2:26:1551:0:14:72:323:701:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:C:Taxation and the International Mobility of Inventors
2:27:1603:14:14:72:351:687:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:C:Ufuk Akcigit, Salomé Baslandze, and Stefanie Stantcheva
2:28:1658:14:14:72:234:673:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:C:NBER Working Paper No. 21024
2:29:1686:14:15:72:244:659:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:C:March 2015, Revised October 2015
2:30:1718:15:28:72:272:644:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:C:JEL No. F22,H21,H24,H31,J61,O33,O38
2:31:1753:28:28:273:338:616:12:Times:12:Times:?:ABSTRACT
2:32:1761:28:14:72:540:588:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:F:This paper studies the effect of top tax rates on inventors' international mobility since 1977. We put
2:33:1863:14:14:72:540:574:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:F:special emphasis on “superstar” inventors, those with the most abundant and most valuable patents.
2:34:1961:14:14:72:540:560:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:F:We use panel data on inventors from the United States and European Patent Offices to track inventors'
2:35:2062:14:14:72:540:546:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:F:locations over time and combine it with international effective top tax rate data. We construct a detailed
2:36:2168:14:14:72:540:532:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:F:set of proxies for inventors' counterfactual incomes in each possible destination country including,
2:37:2268:14:14:72:540:518:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:F:among others, measures of patent quality and technological fit with each potential destination. Exploiting
2:38:2374:14:14:72:540:504:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:F:the differential impact of changes in the top tax rate on inventors of different qualities, we find that
2:39:2478:14:14:72:540:490:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:F:superstar top 1% inventors are significantly affected by top tax rates when deciding where to locate.
2:40:2579:14:14:72:540:476:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:F:The elasticity to the net-of-tax rate of the number of domestic superstar inventors is relatively small,
2:41:2683:14:14:72:540:462:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:F:around 0.03, while the elasticity of the number of foreign superstar inventors is around 1. Inventors
2:42:2784:14:14:72:540:448:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:F:who work in multinational companies are more likely to take advantage of tax differentials. On the
2:43:2882:14:14:72:540:434:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:F:other hand, if the company of an inventor has a higher share of its research activity in a given country,
2:44:2987:14:42:72:351:420:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:C:the inventor is less sensitive to the tax rate in that country.
2:45:3050:42:14:72:136:378:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:C:Ufuk Akcigit
2:46:3062:14:14:72:198:364:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:C:Department of Economics
2:47:3085:14:14:72:179:350:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:C:University of Chicago
2:48:3106:14:14:72:175:336:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:C:1126 East 59th Street
2:49:3127:14:14:72:180:322:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:C:Saieh Hall, Office 403
2:50:3149:14:14:72:162:308:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:C:Chicago, IL 60637
2:51:3166:14:14:72:124:294:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:C:and NBER
2:52:3174:14:28:72:185:280:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:C:uakcigit@uchicago.edu
2:53:3195:28:14:72:160:252:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:C:Salomé Baslandze

3:66:3440:0:28:72:185:701:14:g_d0_f2:14:g_d0_f2:C:1    Introduction
3:67:3457:28:16:72:540:673:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:In 1876, Alexander Graham Bell invented the telephone, and created the Bell Telephone Company
3:68:3550:16:17:72:540:657:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:one year later.  By 1886, more than 150,000 people in the United States owned telephones.  In 1916,
3:69:3649:17:16:72:540:640:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:James L. Kraft patented a pasteurization technique for cheese and established his company, Kraft
3:70:3745:16:16:72:540:624:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:Foods Inc., that would grow into a conglomerate responsible for creating some of the United States’
3:71:3844:16:17:72:540:608:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:most popular food products and employing more than 100,000 people.  In 1968, Ralph Baer created
3:72:3939:17:16:72:540:591:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:a TV game unit that allowed players to control on-screen action with paddle controls.  Today, the
3:73:4036:16:17:72:540:575:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:video gaming industry is worth $66 billion.  In the early 1970s, Michael Ter-Pogossian developed
3:74:4132:17:16:72:540:558:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:the positron emission tomography (PET) scanner, used today in countless medical examinations.
3:75:4225:16:17:72:540:542:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:In the mid-1970s, Samar Basu, through a series of patents, invented the technology that allowed
3:76:4320:17:16:72:540:525:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:the lithium ion batteries used in innumerable consumer products to be recharged multiple times.
3:77:4415:16:16:72:540:509:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:In 1981, Charles Simonyi started developing some of Microsoft Office’s most profitable products.
3:78:4511:16:17:72:540:493:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:In addition to being very prolific inventors, these innovators had something else in common:  they
3:79:4609:17:17:72:168:476:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:were allimmigrants.
3:80:4628:17:16:88:539:459:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:According to World Intellectual Property Organization data, inventors are highly mobile geo-
3:81:4720:16:17:72:540:443:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:graphically with a migration rate around 8%.1But what determines their patterns of migration?
3:82:4813:17:16:72:540:426:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:In particular, how does tax policy affect migration?  The fear of a “brain drain” and the exodus of
3:83:4912:16:17:72:540:410:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:economically valuable agents in response to higher taxation has led to a vivid public debate regard-
3:84:5012:17:16:72:540:393:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:ing the taxation of high income people.  For instance, in response to the New York Times’ (Feb,
3:85:5107:16:16:72:540:377:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:2013) article entitled “The Myth of the Rich Who Flee From Taxes,”2following Gerard Depardieu’s
3:86:5202:16:17:72:540:361:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:Russian exodus for tax purposes,  Forbes issued an article entitled “Sorry New York Times,  Tax
3:87:5297:17:16:72:539:344:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:Flight of the Rich Is Not a Myth.”3In this paper, we study the effects of top income taxes on the
3:88:5394:16:17:72:465:328:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:international migration of inventors, who are key drivers of technological progress.
3:89:5478:17:17:88:539:311:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:While an important issue, international migration responses to taxation have remained under-
3:90:5570:17:16:72:540:294:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:explored due to the lack of a large-scale international panel dataset.  One important exception is
3:91:5668:16:16:72:540:278:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:the  study  of  the  migration  responses  of  football  players,  a  set  of  economic  agents  very  different
3:92:5780:16:17:72:540:262:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:from inventors, byKleven, Landais, and Saez (2013).  In our analysis, we use a unique international
3:93:5879:17:16:72:540:245:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:panel data on all inventors from the U.S. and European patent offices in an unusual way, namely to
3:94:5977:16:17:72:540:229:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:track the international location of inventors since the 1970s.  The benchmark data is a panel data
3:95:6075:17:16:72:539:212:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:from the Disambiguated Inventor Data byLaiet al.(2012), based on inventors who patent with
3:96:6165:16:17:72:540:196:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:the United States Patent Office (USPTO). The focus is on the 8 OECD countries that represent
3:97:6257:17:16:72:540:179:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:the bulk of USPTO patents for the period 1977-2000:  Canada, France, Germany, Great Britain,
3:98:6349:16:16:72:540:163:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:Italy, Japan, Switzerland, and the United States.  The new disambiguated European inventor data
3:99:6444:16:17:72:540:147:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:is fromCoffano and Tarasconi(2014).  The U.S. and European patent offices together account for
3:100:6538:17:17:72:540:130:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:a  very  large  fraction  of  worldwide  patents,  so  that  our  sample  contains  most  of  the  universe  of
3:101:6649:17:15:84:540:113:6:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f7:F:1For a recent study using this data, seeMiguelez and Fink(2013).  High skilled workers are in general more mobile
3:102:6762:15:7:71:407:98:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:F:that low skilled workers, with inventors being among most high-skilled immigrants.
3:103:6844:7:11:84:325:91:6:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f7:A:2Article by James B. Stewart, published February 15, 2013.
3:104:6902:11:0:84:346:80:6:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f7:A:3Article by Paul Roderick Gregory, published February 17, 2013.
4:105:7000:0:16:72:540:701:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:inventors who patent.  We combine this inventor data with international effective marginal top tax
4:106:7098:16:17:72:323:685:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:rate data from Piketty, Saez, and Stantcheva (2014).
4:107:7150:17:16:88:539:668:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:Particularly interesting are “superstar” inventors, namely those with the most abundant and
4:108:7241:16:17:72:540:652:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:most valuable innovations.  The distribution of inventor quality, as captured by the citations that
4:109:7340:17:16:72:540:635:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:an inventor’s patents receive– an often-used measure of the economic value of patents – is highly
4:110:7437:16:17:72:540:619:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:skewed:4As can be seen in Figure 1, while the median and mean inventors have, respectively, 11
4:111:7531:17:21:72:468:602:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:and 42 lifetime citations, the average top 1% superstar inventor has 1019 citations.

4:130:8132:11:11:72:540:271:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:F:Patent Office data 1977-2000 from 8 countries:  Canada, Great Britain, Germany, France, Italy, Japan, Switzerland,

4:132:8371:11:21:72:183:249:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:F:of the data, see Section2.3.
4:133:8399:21:16:88:539:228:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:There are three major challenges that arise when studying the migration responses to taxation.
4:134:8493:16:16:72:540:212:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:These  challenges  come  in  addition  to  the  aforementioned  usual  obstacle  of  lack  of  international
4:135:8601:16:17:72:540:196:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:panel data – a hurdle we are able to resolve in this paper thanks to the use of the patent data.
4:136:8697:17:16:72:540:179:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:First, conceptually, migration decisions should depend on thecounterfactualincome that an agent
4:137:8792:16:17:72:540:163:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:expects to receive in each potential location, which is naturally not observed.  Second, migration
4:138:8890:17:16:72:540:146:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:decisions should depend on the counterfactual average tax rate that the agent expects to pay in each
4:139:8990:16:17:72:540:130:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:potential location, which itself depends on the (unknown) counterfactual income earned.  Finally,
4:140:9087:17:16:72:488:113:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:average tax rates may be endogenous to other factors in a country and in a given year.
4:141:9173:16:17:88:539:97:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:Our  strategy  to  study  mobility  proceeds  in  three  steps  in  order  to  address  these  three  chal-
4:142:9280:17:0:84:380:80:6:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f7:A:4See Section 2.3for references to the literature studying patent citations.
5:143:9408:0:16:72:540:701:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:lenges, making use of some unique features of the patent data.  First, we construct detailed proxies
5:144:9508:16:17:72:540:685:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:for inventors’ counterfactual earnings in each potential destination country, which include, among
5:145:9606:17:16:72:540:668:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:others, measures of inventors’ qualities.  Indeed, the patent data provides us with a rare opportu-
5:146:9705:16:16:72:540:652:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:nity to directly measure inventor productivity and quality.  Our benchmark measure of quality is
5:147:9801:16:17:72:540:636:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:citations-adjusted patents, but we also consider the number of patents, average citations per patent,
5:148:9902:17:16:72:540:619:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:the maximum citations per patent, as well as measures of the breadth of patents and breadth of
5:149:9996:16:17:72:540:603:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:impact of an inventor.5We focus on inventors who are employees of companies and, hence, not the
5:150:10091:17:17:71:184:586:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:owners of their patents.
5:151:10115:17:17:88:539:569:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:The  quality  measures  based  on  citations,  are  important  determinants  of  inventors’  incomes,
5:152:10216:17:16:71:539:552:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:directly and indirectly.  Directly, more citations mean a higher economic value of the patent (Tra-
5:153:10315:16:17:71:539:536:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:jtenberg, 1990) and companies would typically reward inventors through bonuses or “fair-share”
5:154:10409:17:16:71:539:519:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:agreements.  Indirectly, employers should try to promote and retain their star employees, as char-
5:155:10507:16:16:71:539:503:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:acterized by high patent qualities (see also the papers reviewed in Section2.4which document the
5:156:10603:16:18:71:275:487:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:link between patent citations and income).
5:157:10645:18:16:88:539:469:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:In addition to inventor quality, we also proxy for counterfactual earnings through a variety of
5:158:10740:16:17:71:539:453:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:variables, such as inventors’ technological field, their technological fit with each potential destina-
5:159:10843:17:16:71:539:436:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:tion country, their tenure, and ability-technological field-country specific trends.  We also exploit
5:160:10944:16:17:71:539:420:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:information about what type of institution the inventor works for, notably whether he is employed
5:161:11041:17:16:71:539:403:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:by  a  multinational,  and  the  share  of  the  innovative  activity  of  his  company  performed  in  each
5:162:11149:16:18:71:212:387:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:potential destination country.
5:163:11179:18:16:88:539:369:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:Based on our benchmark quality measure (and for each of the other measures), we construct
5:164:11268:16:16:71:539:353:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:a corresponding quality distribution, conditional on region of origin and year, and determine the
5:165:11365:16:17:71:540:337:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:rank of each inventor in this distribution.6We define superstar inventors as those in the top 1%
5:166:11461:17:16:71:539:320:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:of the quality distribution, and similarly construct the top 1-5%, the top 5-10%, and subsequent
5:167:11557:16:18:71:150:304:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:quality brackets.
5:168:11574:18:16:88:539:286:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:Second, regarding the counterfactual average tax rate, we focus on the elasticity of migration
5:169:11668:16:17:71:539:270:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:to the top marginal income tax rate.  The resulting elasticity is a reduced form parameter and our
5:170:11766:17:16:71:539:253:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:estimates are not necessarily interpretable as the “elasticities of migration to net-of-tax income,”
5:171:11866:16:17:71:539:237:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:for several reasons.  First, top marginal tax rates are not equal to effective top average tax rates
5:172:11966:17:16:71:539:220:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:because of the nonlinearity of the tax system.  This should be a minimal concern in the case of
5:173:12061:16:16:71:539:204:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:very  high  earners  who  are  well  above  the  top  tax  bracket.   Second,  there  are  other  potentially
5:174:12170:16:21:71:540:188:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:relevant taxes for inventors, such as capital or corporate taxes.7To minimize the latter concern,
5:175:12267:21:14:84:539:167:6:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f7:F:5See Section 2.3 for a detailed description of how we construct quality measures for inventors and for alternative
5:176:12381:14:8:72:180:153:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:F:definitions of “superstars.”
5:177:12409:8:14:84:539:145:6:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f7:F:6The  three  benchmark  regions  used  to  construct  the  per  region  and  year  quality  distributions  are  based  on
5:178:12530:14:11:72:540:131:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:F:comparable patenting intensities.  They are i) the U.S., ii) European countries and Canada, and iii) Japan, but we
5:179:12644:11:7:72:385:120:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:F:also use per-country rankings for robustness checks (in Appendix TableA16).
5:180:12719:7:15:84:540:113:6:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f7:F:7Note however that we are not trying to understand the effects of the taxation ofdirectpatent income (such as
5:181:12828:15:11:72:540:98:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:F:royalties or corporate income).  We are instead interested in the taxation of salary and bonus earnings,  for which
5:182:12943:11:11:72:540:87:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:F:personal income taxes are the main consideration.  Appendix TableA14shows that the effect of capital gains taxes
5:183:13055:11:0:72:335:76:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:F:on migration is insignificant once income taxes are controlled for.
6:184:13157:0:16:72:540:701:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:we restrict our benchmark sample to those inventors who are employees of companies and who are
6:185:13251:16:17:72:540:685:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:not the assignees of the patents – this ensures that personal ordinary income tax should be the
6:186:13346:17:16:72:539:668:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:main tax affecting decisions.8Furthermore, firms’ decisions and institutional factors (such as the
6:187:13444:16:16:72:540:652:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:visa system) influence the response to taxes.  Incidentally, the estimated elasticity to the top tax
6:188:13544:16:19:72:449:636:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:rate may also be interestingper seas it captures the effects of a “success” tax.
6:189:13624:19:16:88:539:617:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:Third, turning to the identification, the simplest strategy is to exploit variation in top marginal
6:190:13723:16:17:71:539:601:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:tax  rates  across  time  and  countries,  controlling  for  country  fixed  effects,  year  fixed  effects,  and
6:191:13836:17:16:71:539:584:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:country  specific  linear  trends  to  filter  out  longer-term  country-specific  evolutions  in  innovation,
6:192:13946:16:17:71:539:568:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:incomes, and migration.  We do this analysis merely as a first pass as there may be other factors
6:193:14043:17:16:71:539:551:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:correlated with top marginal tax rates which vary at the same time in a given country.  Instead,
6:194:14139:16:16:71:539:535:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:our preferred identification filters out all country-year level variation and exploits the differential
6:195:14242:16:17:71:539:519:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:impact of changes in the top marginal tax rate on top superstar inventors and slightly lower quality
6:196:14342:17:16:71:539:502:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:inventors within a given country and year.  Top 1% inventors and those of slightly lower qualities are
6:197:14444:16:17:71:539:486:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:similar enough to be subject to the same country-year level policies and economic effects.  However,
6:198:14544:17:16:71:539:469:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:only inventors who are actually in the top bracket are directly affected by the changes in top tax
6:199:14642:16:17:71:539:453:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:rates.   The  evidence  presented  suggests  that  top  1%  superstar  inventors  are  well  in  the  top  tax
6:200:14752:17:16:71:539:436:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:bracket.  While the top 1-5% are still very likely to be in the top bracket, the likelihood of being
6:201:14852:16:16:71:539:420:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:in the top tax bracket declines sharply as we move down through the top 5-10% to the top 10-25%
6:202:14947:16:17:71:539:404:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:or below top 25% inventors.9Hence, the lower quality, top 5-10%, top 10-25%, and below top 25%
6:203:15041:17:18:72:331:387:11:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f5:B:groups serve as control groups for the top 1% group.10
6:204:15095:18:17:88:539:369:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:We perform the analysis at three, successively more detailed levels.  We start by documenting
6:205:15188:17:16:72:540:352:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:some stylized macroeconomic facts about the relation between mobility and top tax rates.  Since
6:206:15283:16:17:72:540:336:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:the  1970s  there  is  a  negative  correlation  between  the  top  tax  rate  and  the  share  of  top  quality
6:207:15395:17:16:72:540:319:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:foreign inventors who locate in a country,  as well as the share of top quality domestic inventors
6:208:15493:16:19:72:238:303:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:who remain in their home country.
6:209:15526:19:16:88:539:284:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:Delving  deeper  into  three  specific  case  studies,  we  exploit  the  quasi-experimental  variation
6:210:15629:16:24:72:540:268:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:provided  by  migration  or  tax  reforms.   First,  we  consider  the  special  case  of  Russian  inventors–
6:211:15739:24:11:84:530:244:6:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f7:A:8We also check that our results hold for the full sample which includes non-employees in Appendix Table A16.
6:212:15847:11:15:84:539:233:6:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f7:F:9As explained in Section 5.1, “below top 25%” refers here to a relatively high quality group of inventors who at
6:213:15959:15:7:72:420:218:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:F:some point have been or will be in the top 25%, but are not currently in the top 25%.
6:214:16044:7:15:80:539:211:6:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f7:F:10Conceptually,  this  main  identification  strategy  is  akin  to  a  “fuzzy  regression  discontinuity  design,”  where  the
6:215:16171:15:11:72:540:196:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:F:quality ranking generates a fuzzy threshold above which inventors are “treated” by the top tax rate changes.  The
6:216:16284:11:11:72:540:185:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:F:design is fuzzy because we do not know counterfactual income and use quality rankings instead. This is similar in spirit
6:217:16404:11:11:72:540:174:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:F:to papers using the differential impact of tax changes across income tax brackets (Eissa, 1995) or across households
6:218:16520:11:10:72:540:163:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:F:with different non-labor income and family size (Eissa and Hoynes, 2006) rather than quality brackets like we do.
6:219:16633:10:11:72:540:153:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:F:It is most closely related to the differential propensities of being “treated,” as inHoynes and Schanzenbach(2009)
6:220:16747:11:11:72:540:142:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:F:orHoynes and Schanzenbach(2012) who multiply Food Stamp program introduction by propensity to participate
6:221:16852:11:11:71:539:131:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:F:(proxied by group-level food stamp participation): in our case, we interact the top tax rate with the inventor’s quality
6:222:16972:11:11:71:539:120:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:F:ranking (which proxies the propensity of being in the top bracket).  When choosing the control group for top 1%
6:223:17083:11:11:71:539:109:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:F:inventors, there is a trade-off between maximizing comparability (i.e., choosing a group very close in quality e.g., the
6:224:17203:11:11:71:539:98:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:F:top 5-10%) and minimizing the control group’s propensity of being treated (i.e., choosing a group further down the
6:225:17317:11:11:71:539:87:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:F:quality distribution, e.g., the below top 25%).  We therefore report the estimated coefficients for all inventor quality
6:226:17437:11:0:71:414:76:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:F:groups and the implied elasticities relative to three different choices of control group.
7:227:17579:0:16:72:540:701:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:a group whose migration opportunities were severely restricted before the collapse of the Soviet
7:228:17675:16:17:72:540:685:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:Union.   We  show  that,  in  accordance  with  our  main  identification  strategy,  top  quality  Russian
7:229:17782:17:16:72:540:668:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:inventors, relative to lower quality Russian inventors, tended to migrate to lower top tax countries
7:230:17882:16:16:72:540:652:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:after  the  Soviet  Union  collapsed.   We  then  exploit  two  large  tax  reforms,  namely  the  U.S.  Tax
7:231:17990:16:18:72:409:636:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:reform Act of 1986 and Denmark’s “Researchers’ Tax” reform of 1992.
7:232:18057:18:17:88:539:618:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:Finally, we estimate a full-fledged multinomial location choice model to obtain the micro elas-
7:233:18152:17:16:72:540:601:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:ticities to top tax rates for foreign and domestic inventors.  We use the two identification strategies
7:234:18255:16:17:72:540:585:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:previously described exploiting, first, country-by-year variation in top tax rates and, second, the
7:235:18354:17:18:72:443:568:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:differential effective impact of top tax rates on inventors of different qualities.
7:236:18437:18:16:88:539:550:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:We find that the superstar top 1% inventors are significantly affected by top tax rates when
7:237:18529:16:17:72:540:534:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:choosing where to locate.  As explained in the text, we provide the effects relative to several possible
7:238:18633:17:16:72:540:517:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:control groups for the top 1% inventors.  At the lower end, using the top 5-10% as a control group
7:239:18731:16:17:72:540:501:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:yields an elasticity of the number of domestic superstar top 1% inventors to the net-of-tax rate of
7:240:18830:17:16:72:540:484:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:0.02, which, as explained below, may be a lower bound.  Using the top 10-25% or the below top 25%
7:241:18927:16:16:72:540:468:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:as control groups yields elasticities of, respectively, 0.02 and 0.03.  On the other hand, the elasticity
7:242:19032:16:17:72:540:452:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:of  the  number  of  foreign  top  1%  superstar  inventors  to  the  net-of-tax  rate  is  much  larger,  with
7:243:19143:17:16:72:540:435:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:corresponding values of 0.63, 0.84, and 1.  To put these numbers into perspective, the elasticity of
7:244:19243:16:17:72:540:419:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:the number of domestic football players inKleven, Landais, and Saez (2013)to the net-of-tax rate
7:245:19339:17:16:72:540:402:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:ranges from 0.07 to 0.16 depending on the specification, and the elasticity of the number of foreign
7:246:19439:16:17:72:540:386:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:players ranges from 0.6 to 1.3.  We also find some evidence consistent with sorting by ability and
7:247:19537:17:18:72:227:369:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:general equilibrium wage effects.
7:248:19570:18:16:88:539:351:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:The  type  and  structure  of  companies  seems  important  for  the  migration  decision:  Inventors
7:249:19671:16:17:72:540:335:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:who have worked for multinationals in the previous period are more likely to take advantage of tax
7:250:19769:17:16:72:540:318:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:differentials.  On the contrary,  they are much less sensitive to the tax rate in a given country if
7:251:19869:16:18:72:447:302:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:their company has a significant share of its innovative activity in that country.
7:252:19950:18:17:88:539:284:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:We then perform extensive robustness checks on these benchmark results.  First, we consider
7:253:20041:17:16:72:540:267:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:five  different  measures  of  inventor  quality,  both  static  and  dynamic,  and  alternative  proxies  for
7:254:20151:16:16:72:540:251:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:earnings.  Second, we contrast short-term and long-term mobility in response to taxation.  Third,
7:255:20248:16:17:72:540:235:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:we  address  potential  selection  based  on  patenting  behavior  by  estimating  a  Heckman  selection
7:256:20352:17:16:72:540:218:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:model that exploits a 1994 reform effectively expanding patent protection in the U.S. Finally, we
7:257:20449:16:17:72:540:202:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:reproduce the analysis on the disambiguated inventor data from the European Patent Office and
7:258:20542:17:16:72:540:185:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:find very similar elasticities of the number of domestic and foreign top 1% superstar inventors to
7:259:20640:16:27:72:307:169:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:the net-of-tax rate of, respectively, 0.02 and 0.76.
7:260:20692:27:17:72:539:142:11:g_d0_f14:11:g_d0_f3:B:Related  Literature:That  high  skilled  migration  and  its  drivers  are  important  considerations
7:261:20793:17:16:72:539:125:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:has been highlighted in the literature (see the paper byKerr(2013) and the extensive references
7:262:20888:16:17:71:539:109:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:therein).   High-skilled  immigrants  account  for  roughly  25%  of  U.S.  workers  in  innovation  and
7:263:20992:17:16:71:539:92:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:entrepreneurship and contribute disproportionately to patents or start-ups.  Immigrants account
7:264:21087:16:0:71:539:76:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:for a majority of the net increase in the U.S. STEM workforce since 1995.  There seems to be a
8:265:21216:0:16:72:539:701:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:positive  selection  among  immigrants,  as  documented  byGrogger  and  Hanson(2011)  for  foreign
8:266:21315:16:17:72:540:685:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:Ph.D. students who stay in the U.S. and byChiquiar and Hanson(2005) for Mexican immigrant
8:267:21404:17:17:72:111:668:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:workers.
8:268:21412:17:17:88:539:651:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:In  turn,  not  just  the  receiving,  but  also  the  sending  country  is  affected.   It  could  either  be
8:269:21522:17:16:72:540:634:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:suffering from a “brain drain,”  by losing highly skilled people or gaining from a “brain gain,”  if
8:270:21622:16:16:72:540:618:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:people invest in human capital more with the prospect of immigration or from remittances.  Indeed,
8:271:21720:16:17:72:540:602:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:oversea diasporas have been studied as important determinants of knowledge flows (Foley and Kerr,
8:272:21817:17:16:72:540:585:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:2013).  Inventor migration and the formation of geographical knowledge clusters and their spillovers
8:273:21917:16:17:72:539:569:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:have also received attention (Miguelez and Moreno(2014),Miguelez(2013),Breschi, Lissoni, and
8:274:22009:17:17:72:286:552:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:Tarasconi (2014)and the references therein).
8:275:22053:17:17:88:539:535:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:Our  paper  adds  to  a  recent  literature  that  studies  the  international  migration  of  people  in
8:276:22158:17:16:72:540:518:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:response to taxation.  Most closely related are the papers byKleven, Landais, Saez, and Schultz
8:277:22253:16:17:72:539:502:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:(2014)andKleven,  Landais,  and  Saez  (2013).Kleven,  Landais,  Saez,  and  Schultz  (2014)find
8:278:22349:17:16:72:540:485:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:very high elasticities of the number of high income foreigners in Denmark using a preferential tax
8:279:22447:16:17:72:540:469:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:scheme on high-earning foreigners implemented by Denmark in 1992 that reduced top tax rates for
8:280:22542:17:16:72:540:452:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:3 years.11Kleven, Landais, and Saez (2013)study the migration of football players across European
8:281:22639:16:17:72:540:436:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:clubs.  While we find somewhat lower elasticities for domestic inventors,Kleven, Landais, and Saez
8:282:22737:17:16:72:539:419:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:(2013)themselves conjectured that football players might be substantially more mobile than other
8:283:22833:16:16:72:540:403:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:high-skilled workers, because they earn most of their lifetime income over a short period and their
8:284:22932:16:17:72:540:387:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:profession  involves  little  country-specific  capital.   In  addition,  their  sample  exclusively  considers
8:285:23043:17:16:72:540:370:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:migration across European countries, while we also include the United States, Canada, and Japan.
8:286:23139:16:17:72:540:354:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:Expanding the study to other continents might,  one would expect,  reduce the tax elasticities of
8:287:23236:17:16:72:539:337:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:migration.  Other related papers consider migration within countries.Bakija and Slemrod(2004)
8:288:23329:16:17:72:540:321:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:use Federal Estate Tax returns to show that the effect of higher state taxes on the migration of
8:289:23425:17:16:72:539:304:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:wealthy individuals across states in the U.S. is very small.12Moretti and Wilson(2014) consider
8:290:23520:16:16:72:540:288:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:aggregate state level effects of adopting subsidies for biotech employers –such as increase in R&D
8:291:23618:16:17:72:540:272:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:tax incentives– on the inflows of star scientists.  Very complementary to our paper is the recent
8:292:23715:17:16:72:540:255:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:creative  paper  byMoretti  and  Wilson(2015)  which  considers  the  effects  of  state  taxes  on  the
8:293:23819:16:17:72:540:239:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:migration of star scientists across U.S. states and also finds highly significant effects of taxes on
8:294:23920:17:17:72:121:222:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:migration.
8:295:23930:17:17:88:539:205:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:Estimating  the  elasticity  of  migration  to  the  tax  rate  is  also  important  for  the  theoretical
8:296:24036:17:16:72:540:188:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:literature of optimal taxation with migration, as it enters the optimal tax formulas (Mirrlees,1982;
8:297:24136:16:17:72:539:172:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:Wilson,1980,1982).13Our paper can shed some light on how big the proposed modifications to
8:298:24226:17:21:72:499:155:11:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f5:B:standard optimal tax formulas have to be empirically in order to account for migration.14
8:299:24315:21:14:80:539:134:6:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f7:F:11By contrast, Young and Varner(2011) study the effects of a change in the millionaire tax rate in New Jersey on
8:300:24427:14:7:71:218:120:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:F:migration and find small elasticities.
8:301:24465:7:11:80:531:113:6:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f7:A:12Liebig et al.(2007) study mobility within Switzerland, across cantons and find small sensitivities to tax rates.
8:302:24579:11:15:80:540:102:6:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f7:F:13See also the more recent papers bySimula and Trannoy(2010) and especiallyLehmann et al.(2014) who consider
8:303:24687:15:7:72:330:87:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:F:optimal nonlinear income taxation in the presence of migration.
8:304:24750:7:0:80:539:80:6:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f7:F:14The same applies for the macro structural literature that includes migration channels and needs to calibrate the
9:305:24917:0:16:88:540:701:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:The rest of the paper is organized as follows.  Section2 presents the setting and data, as well
9:306:25012:16:17:72:540:685:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:as a simple model of inventor migration.  Section3 shows some stylized macro facts on the relation
9:307:25110:17:16:71:539:668:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:between top tax rates and superstar inventors’ migration.  Section4 presents quasi-experimental
9:308:25205:16:16:72:540:652:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:evidence based on three country case studies.  Section5 describes the multinomial location model
9:309:25301:16:17:72:540:636:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:estimation  and  the  main  results.   Section6  contains  several  robustness  checks  and  extensions.
9:310:25405:17:16:72:539:619:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:Section7 repeats the analysis on inventors who patent with the European Patent Office.  Section8
9:311:25501:16:40:71:120:603:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:concludes.
9:312:25511:40:28:71:291:563:14:g_d0_f2:14:g_d0_f2:C:2    Setting, Data, and Strategy
9:313:25543:28:16:71:539:535:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:This section provides some background information on inventors, patents, and our various datasets.
9:314:25641:16:16:71:539:519:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:We explain how we use the unique features of patent data for the study of the effects of taxation
9:315:25738:16:34:71:400:503:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:on inventor mobility with the help of a simple location choice model.
9:316:25807:34:24:71:310:469:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:C:2.1    Inventors and patents:  Background
9:317:25848:24:16:71:539:445:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:Inventors are the authors of innovations.  They can be employees of companies, work for research
9:318:25944:16:17:71:539:429:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:institutions, or be self-employed “garage inventors.”  Patents protect the intellectual property of the
9:319:26047:17:16:71:539:412:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:innovation.  They are legally granted to an assignee.  The assignee is either an individual (possibly,
9:320:26149:16:17:71:539:396:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:but not necessarily, one of the inventors on a given patent), a national, local, or state government,
9:321:26250:17:16:71:355:379:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:an institute, a hospital or medical institute, or a university.
9:322:26313:16:17:88:539:363:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:Inventors  seem  to  be  more  mobile  than  the  general  population,  which  is  consistent  with  a
9:323:26415:17:16:71:540:346:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:positively documented relation between skill and mobility.  As summarized inMiguelez and Fink
9:324:26508:16:17:71:539:330:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:(2013), the global migration rate in 2000 for the population above 25 years old was 1.8%, ranging
9:325:26605:17:16:71:539:313:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:from 1.1% for the unskilled to 5.4% for those with tertiary education.  In our benchmark sample,
9:326:26701:16:17:71:539:297:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:2.3% of inventors move at least once over their lifetime in the sample (an average of 12 years) and
9:327:26800:17:33:71:365:280:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:4.6% of the superstar inventors move over the same duration.
9:328:26860:33:24:71:330:247:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:C:2.2    A Simple Model of Inventor Migration
9:329:26903:24:17:71:539:223:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:To motivate our empirical analysis, consider the following very simple model of inventor migration.
9:330:27002:17:16:71:539:206:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:There areCcountries, labeled asc∈ {1,...,C}.  The wage of inventoriin countryc′at timetis
9:331:27091:16:16:71:539:190:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:denoted bywic′t.  Let   ̃wic′tdenote the corresponding marginal product.  Indexiallows the marginal
9:332:27190:16:17:71:539:174:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:product to depend on several inventor characteristics, such as his technological class, his age, as
9:333:27289:17:16:71:539:157:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:well as characteristics of the firm or employer he works for.  If the international labor market is
9:334:27388:16:17:71:515:141:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:perfectly competitive, each inventor is paid his marginal product, so that   ̃wic′t=wic′t,∀c′,t,i.
9:335:27486:17:16:88:540:124:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:Suppose that in countryc, an inventor with home countryhihas to pay a tax rateτchiton his
9:336:27575:16:21:71:540:108:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:total income at timet.  The tax rate is allowed to depend on the country of origin because foreigners
9:337:27676:21:11:72:539:87:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:F:migration elasticities (seeCosar, Guner, and Tybout (2010)).  The migration channel could also further bolster recent
9:338:27793:11:0:71:519:76:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:F:findings that the room for higher tax revenue through more progressive taxes is limited inGuneret al.(2014).
10:339:27936:0:16:72:540:701:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:can sometimes face different tax regimes in different countries.  For instance, U.S. citizens are taxed
10:340:28039:16:18:72:201:685:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:on their worldwide income.
10:341:28065:18:16:88:539:667:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:In addition to the income earned, there is also a net utility benefit denotedμictfrom locating
10:342:28159:16:17:72:539:651:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:in countrycat timetfor inventori.  This benefit is person-specific and can include, among others,
10:343:28256:17:16:72:540:634:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:a  home  bias,  technological  strengths  and  characteristics  of  the  country,  language  differences,  or
10:344:28365:16:16:72:540:618:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:distance to the home country.  It can also capture country-specific characteristics of the company
10:345:28463:16:17:72:540:602:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:the inventor works for, such as the share of innovative activities the company performs in country
10:346:28561:17:18:72:167:585:11:g_d0_f15:11:g_d0_f3:B:cat any given time.
10:347:28580:18:34:88:435:567:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:Total utility from choosing countrycat timetfor inventoriis given by:
10:348:28649:34:0:236:271:533:11:g_d0_f15:11:g_d0_f15:C:Uict=u
10:349:28655:0:9:273:278:542:11:g_d0_f21:11:g_d0_f21:?:(
10:350:28656:9:0:278:370:533:11:g_d0_f15:8:g_d0_f18:?:wict(1−τchit) +μict
10:351:28675:0:34:370:375:542:11:g_d0_f21:11:g_d0_f21:?:)
10:352:28676:34:17:88:539:508:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:If  to  a  first  order  there  are  no  adjustment  costs  of  moving,  the  decision  of  where  to  locate
10:353:28785:17:16:72:539:491:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:every  period  is  history-independent.   Hence,  countrycwill  be  chosen  in  periodtif  and  only  if
10:354:28889:16:0:72:78:475:11:g_d0_f15:11:g_d0_f15:C:u
10:355:28890:0:9:80:85:484:11:g_d0_f21:11:g_d0_f21:A:(
10:356:28891:9:0:85:176:475:11:g_d0_f15:8:g_d0_f18:A:wict(1−τchit) +μict
10:357:28910:0:9:176:181:484:11:g_d0_f21:11:g_d0_f21:?:)
10:358:28911:9:0:184:235:475:11:g_d0_f16:6:g_d0_f19:?:∈argmaxc′
10:359:28920:0:9:238:244:484:11:g_d0_f21:11:g_d0_f21:?:{
10:360:28921:9:0:245:251:475:11:g_d0_f15:11:g_d0_f15:C:u
10:361:28922:0:9:253:258:484:11:g_d0_f21:11:g_d0_f21:?:(
10:362:28923:9:0:258:357:475:11:g_d0_f15:8:g_d0_f18:?:wic′t(1−τc′hit) +μic′t
10:363:28945:0:9:357:368:484:11:g_d0_f21:11:g_d0_f21:?:)}
10:364:28947:9:18:368:371:475:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:?:.
10:365:28948:18:16:88:539:457:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:This dispenses us from having to make potentially unrealistic assumptions about the expecta-
10:366:29040:16:16:72:540:441:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:tions of future tax rates, on which there is little empirical evidence and which could be country-
10:367:29138:16:17:72:540:425:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:specific.  Note that for any two countries, none of which is the home country of the inventor, the
10:368:29236:17:16:72:540:408:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:utility  from  living  in  one  of  these  countries  does  not  depend  on  the  other  country  –  this  is  the
10:369:29350:16:17:72:540:392:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:sense  in  which  there  are  no  adjustment  costs.   However,  the  utility  from  living  in  any  country
10:370:29459:17:16:72:540:375:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:does depend on the home country, for instance, through a home bias, geographical distance to or
10:371:29554:16:17:72:540:359:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:language differences with the home country (which are the factors we control for in the estimation).
10:372:29654:17:16:72:540:342:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:In that sense, the home country plays a special role because it enters as a time-invariant individual
10:373:29755:16:18:72:235:326:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:characteristic through the indexi.
10:374:29789:18:16:88:539:308:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:The model highlights that, conceptually, it is the average tax that should matter for the supply
10:375:29885:16:17:72:540:292:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:of inventors in a country.  The probability that inventorilocates in countrycwill normally depend
10:376:29982:17:16:72:539:275:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:on the full vector of tax rates in all countries, (τ1hit,...,τchit,....,τChit).  However, for the empirical
10:377:30089:16:16:72:540:259:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:analysis,  we  make  the  assumption  that  the  tax  rate  of  any  other  country  only  has  a  negligible
10:378:30198:16:17:72:539:243:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:impact on the supply of inventors in countryc.  This is a good approximation if there are many
10:379:30292:17:16:72:540:226:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:possible origin and destination countries and each is relatively small.  Hence, to a first order, the
10:380:30393:16:17:72:540:210:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:probability  that  inventors  from  countryklocate  in  countrycwill  depend  only  onτcktand  the
10:381:30491:17:17:72:223:193:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:relationship should be negative.
10:382:30523:17:17:88:539:176:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:Note that the personal location preferences captured byμcould be so strong that they com-
10:383:30612:17:16:72:540:159:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:pletely  dominate  any  considerations  of  tax  differences.   As  a  result,  strong  location  preferences
10:384:30721:16:17:72:540:143:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:unrelated to net income will reduce the observed sensitivity to tax rates.  In the empirical analysis,
10:385:30823:17:16:72:540:126:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:we will explore such factors related to the type of job and company the inventor works in, in addition
10:386:30925:16:18:72:510:110:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:to the standard factors such as home bias, language differences, and geographical distances.
10:387:31017:18:16:88:539:92:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:If the labor market for inventors is not perfectly flexible,  and employers instead have a rigid
10:388:31113:16:0:72:540:76:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:demand for inventors, the wage need not be equal to the marginal product and may be a function
11:389:31260:0:16:72:540:701:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:of the tax system.  This type of general equilibrium effects can be one of the potential reasons for
11:390:31360:16:37:72:437:685:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:endogeneity of top tax rates.  We return to this issue in Sections 5.1 and5.2.
11:391:31438:37:25:72:213:648:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:C:2.3    The Inventor Data
11:392:31462:25:16:72:539:623:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:Our main data source is the Disambiguated Inventor Data (hereafter, DID) byLaiet al.(2012),
11:393:31553:16:17:72:540:607:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:which  identifies  unique  inventors  in  the  U.S.  Patent  Office  (USPTO)  data.   The  USPTO  data
11:394:31655:17:16:72:540:590:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:contains  4.2  million  granted  patents  and  3.1  million  inventors  for  the  period  1975-2010,  which
11:395:31762:16:17:72:426:574:11:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f5:B:represents 18% of worldwide direct patent filings and 26% of all patents.15
11:396:31837:17:17:88:539:557:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:We limit the sample to the 8 major countries which account for 89% of all patents granted by
11:397:31929:17:16:72:540:540:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:the USPTO.16The U.S. accounts for 55% of the USPTO patents, Canada for 2.3%, Great Britain
11:398:32019:16:17:72:540:524:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:for  3%,  Germany  for  7.6%,  Italy  for  1.2%,  Japan  for  19.6%,  France  for  2.9%,  and  Switzerland
11:399:32125:17:16:72:540:507:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:for 1.3%.  These representation differences reflect the different propensities that countries have for
11:400:32227:16:17:72:540:491:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:filing a patent with the USPTO: 58% of U.S. patent filings, 48% of Canadian filings, 19% of British
11:401:32326:17:16:72:540:474:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:filings, 16% of German filings, 20% of Italian filings, 13% of Japanese filings, 17% of French filings,
11:402:32429:16:17:72:324:458:11:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f5:B:and 12% of Swiss filings are filed with the USPTO.17
11:403:32481:17:17:88:539:441:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:But  filing  propensities  and  representation  in  the  patent  data  are  not  necessarily  correlated
11:404:32585:17:16:72:540:424:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:with migration propensities.  Indeed, while it is true that the largest migration corridors are the
11:405:32684:16:17:72:540:408:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:Great Britain-U.S. and Canada-U.S. corridors,  other migration corridors such as the Japan-U.S.
11:406:32779:17:16:72:540:391:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:and Switzerland-U.S. ones are very small, although these countries have a high propensity of filing
11:407:32878:16:17:72:165:375:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:patents in the U.S..
11:408:32898:17:17:88:539:358:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:The DID contains inventors’ disambiguated names and residential address, which allows us to
11:409:32989:17:16:72:540:341:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:track the location of the inventor over time.  Each of the inventor’s patents has a patent number,
11:410:33087:16:16:72:540:325:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:application year, grant year, and assignee name.  In addition, to get information on each patent’s
11:411:33185:16:17:72:540:309:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:characteristics, such as citations or technological class, we merge the inventor data to the NBER
11:412:33282:17:16:72:540:292:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:patent data. Because of the truncation issue for patents’ citations (more recent patents mechanically
11:413:33383:16:17:72:540:276:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:have less time to accumulate citations), we limit the sample to the years 1977-2000. Table1 provides
11:414:33483:17:17:72:295:259:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:some summary statistics for the inventor data.
11:415:33529:17:16:88:539:242:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:Only  very  recently  has  an  effort  of  disambiguation  similar  to  that  done  for  the  DID  been
11:416:33632:16:17:72:540:226:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:undertaken  for  the  European  patent  data  (Coffano  and  Tarasconi(2014),Breschi,  Lissoni,  and
11:417:33732:17:16:72:540:209:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:Tarasconi  (2014)).   Despite  the  fact  that  there  has  been  less  work  on  this  data  and  that  the
11:418:33840:16:17:72:540:193:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:disambiguation algorithm is still less-well established, it offers some good advantages.  The biggest
11:419:33941:17:16:72:540:176:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:of  these  is  that  the  U.S.  is  less  represented  and  European  countries  are  more  represented.   We
11:420:34050:16:17:72:365:160:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:analyze inventor mobility using this data as well in Section7.
11:421:34112:17:20:88:539:143:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:For the macro stylized facts in Section3 and the case studies in Section4, we also use a third
11:422:34206:20:14:80:539:123:6:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f7:F:15Patents can be filed with several offices and a direct patent filing is one of these recorded filings, while a patent
11:423:34325:14:7:72:185:109:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:F:is a given, unique invention.
11:424:34354:7:11:80:491:102:6:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f7:A:16Appendix TableA16shows that our results persist if we do not limit the sample to those countries.
