12:456:36039:14:11:72:540:292:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:F:2000.  The data includes inventors in 8 countries: Canada, France, Germany, Great Britain, Italy, Japan, Switzerland,
12:457:36156:11:11:72:540:281:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:F:and the United States.  The sample contains 4,154,792 observations with 1,868,967 unique inventors.  The benchmark
12:458:36270:11:37:72:381:270:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:F:estimation sample contains all inventors who have ever been in the top 25%.
12:459:36345:37:17:72:539:233:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:alternative data source on inventors’ locations.  This dataset is described in detail byMiguelez and
12:460:36445:17:16:72:540:216:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:Fink(2013) and extracted from patent applications that are filed under the Patent Cooperation
12:461:36538:16:17:72:540:200:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:Treaty (PCT), a treaty administered by the World Intellectual Property Organization (WIPO) that
12:462:36633:17:16:72:540:183:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:offers some advantages for seeking international patent protection.  The PCT data contains 54% of
12:463:36730:16:16:72:540:167:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:all international patent applications, but accounts for only 8% of worldwide patent filings.  However,
12:464:36832:16:17:72:540:151:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:there has been no inventor name disambiguation and it is not yet possible to track inventors by
12:465:36927:17:16:72:540:134:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:name over time in a panel.  As a result, we cannot construct dynamic quality measures for inventors
12:466:37026:16:17:72:540:118:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:as will be described below.  The migration counts could be somewhat biased as, for instance, every
12:467:37124:17:16:72:540:101:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:inventor could be counted several times as a migrant.  However, the great advantage of this dataset
12:468:37223:16:0:72:540:85:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:is that it contains nationality information.  In addition, many smaller countries which are essentially
13:469:37380:0:16:72:540:701:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:non-existent in the DID are better represented in the PCT data, which allows us to provide results
13:470:37478:16:17:72:540:685:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:for a larger set of countries than our benchmark 8 countries.  Thus, this data serves as a robustness
13:471:37579:17:16:72:540:668:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:check on the results using our benchmark data, while also providing an independent and different
13:472:37675:16:31:72:176:652:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:angle for the analysis.
13:473:37698:31:17:72:539:621:11:g_d0_f14:11:g_d0_f3:B:Constructing quality measures for inventors:  Citations received have traditionally been used
13:474:37791:17:16:71:540:604:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:as measures of the economic and technological significance of a patent (seePakes(1986),Pakes and
13:475:37887:16:17:71:540:588:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:Schankerman(1986),Trajtenberg(1990),Harhoff et al.(1999),Hall, Jaffe, and Trajtenberg (2001),
13:476:37980:17:16:71:540:571:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:Bessen(2008),Kogan et al.(2012),Moser et al.(2012),Abrams, Akcigit, and Popadak (2013)).  We
13:477:38072:16:17:71:539:555:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:construct four different dynamic measures of the inventor’s quality, which place different importance
13:478:38173:17:16:71:540:538:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:on the quantity versus value of an inventor’s patents.  Letpijbe the number of truncation-adjusted
13:479:38271:16:16:71:540:522:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:forward citations received by patentjof inventori.  Note that this does not depend on timet, as it
13:480:38369:16:17:71:539:506:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:counts all the forward citations that patent will ever receive, not the citations received until time
13:481:38470:17:16:71:539:489:11:g_d0_f15:11:g_d0_f3:B:t.   The  truncation  adjustment,  which  takes  into  account  the  fact  that  more  recent  patents  have
13:482:38578:16:17:71:539:473:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:less time to accumulate citations, is described inHall, Jaffe, and Trajtenberg (2001).  LetPit−1be
13:483:38676:17:16:71:540:456:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:the set of patents of inventoriby the end of periodt−1.  Our benchmark measure is the lagged
13:484:38768:16:17:71:539:440:11:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f18:B:citations-weighted dynamic patent stock of the inventor.  Formally, we denote this measure byq1it
13:485:38865:17:16:71:156:423:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:and it is equal to:
13:486:38884:16:0:270:295:407:11:g_d0_f15:11:g_d0_f3:?:q1it=
13:487:38889:0:25:305:321:417:11:g_d0_f21:11:g_d0_f21:?:∑
13:488:38890:25:0:299:326:392:8:g_d0_f18:6:g_d0_f6:?:j∈Pit−1
13:489:38897:0:35:328:540:407:11:g_d0_f15:11:g_d0_f3:A:pij(1)
13:490:38903:35:17:71:539:372:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:Measureq1 takes into account both the quantity and the quality of an inventor’s patents, focusing
13:491:39000:17:16:71:539:355:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:on citations accumulated as a measure of one’s influence.  Our second measure, denoted byq2itis
13:492:39095:16:30:71:299:339:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:the lagged patent count of the inventor namely:
13:493:39142:30:30:277:540:309:11:g_d0_f15:11:g_d0_f3:A:q2it=|Pit−1|(2)
13:494:39157:30:16:71:540:279:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:where|Pit−1|is the cardinality of the setPit−1.  This measure ignores the quality of patents and
13:495:39253:16:17:71:539:263:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:purely focuses on their quantity and is hence not our preferred measure.18The third measure,q3it,
13:496:39350:17:35:71:313:246:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:is the lagged mean number of citations per patent:
13:497:39400:35:0:263:288:211:11:g_d0_f15:11:g_d0_f3:?:q3it=
13:498:39405:0:11:293:305:230:11:g_d0_f21:11:g_d0_f21:?:∑
13:499:39406:11:16:304:346:219:8:g_d0_f18:8:g_d0_f18:?:j∈Pit−1pij
13:500:39416:16:0:306:334:203:11:g_d0_f16:11:g_d0_f16:?:|Pit−1|
13:501:39423:0:35:526:540:211:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:(3)
13:502:39426:35:17:71:539:176:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:which measures the average quality of an inventor’s inventions to date.  The fourth measure,q4it,
13:503:39523:17:30:71:409:159:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:is the max number of citations ever received on a patent by inventori:
13:504:39593:30:8:270:322:129:11:g_d0_f15:11:g_d0_f3:?:q4it=  max
13:505:39603:8:0:299:326:121:8:g_d0_f18:6:g_d0_f6:?:j∈Pit−1
13:506:39610:0:38:328:540:129:11:g_d0_f15:11:g_d0_f3:A:pij(4)
13:507:39616:38:15:80:539:91:6:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f7:F:18Many patents have no real economic value and are never cited by any subsequent patent (see for instanceAbrams,
13:508:39728:15:0:72:194:76:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:F:Akcigit, and Popadak (2013)).
14:509:39793:0:16:72:540:701:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:which  captures  the  best  an  inventor  has  ever  achieved  and  whether  he  ever  had  a  “home-run”
14:510:39898:16:17:72:539:685:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:invention.  The additional results for our non-benchmark measuresq2,q3, andq4 are in Section6.
14:511:39992:17:16:88:539:668:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:Based on these quality measures, we can define a ranking for inventors and, in particular, identify
14:512:40091:16:16:72:540:652:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:“superstar” inventors.  We could in principle use a worldwide ranking of inventors.  However, the
14:513:40188:16:17:72:540:636:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:patenting intensity is quite different for different countries and thus the quality measures are not
14:514:40288:17:16:72:540:619:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:necessarily  directly  comparable  at  a  global  level.   This  is  why  we  group  our  8  countries  into  3
14:515:40399:16:17:72:540:603:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:regions based on comparable patenting intensity:  1) the U.S., 2) Japan, 3) European countries and
14:516:40497:17:16:72:540:586:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:Canada.  The U.S. and Japan stand out as the biggest patenting countries with 55% and 26% of all
14:517:40593:16:17:72:539:570:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:granted patents in the sample period (1977-2000).19We assign each inventor to a region based on
14:518:40688:17:16:72:540:553:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:whether his “home” country is in that region.  Since we do not observe actual nationality in this
14:519:40785:16:16:72:540:537:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:data, we call home country the country in which the inventor is first observed in our sample.  We
14:520:40882:16:17:72:540:521:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:define superstars at timetas those in top 1% of the regional quality distribution at timet.The
14:521:40976:17:16:72:540:504:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:top 5%,  top 10%,  and top 25% are calculated in a similar way.  These are dynamic measures in
14:522:41070:16:17:72:540:488:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:the sense that they can change over an inventor’s life, depending on where he falls in the regional
14:523:41169:17:16:72:540:471:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:distribution of quality in any given year.20Henceforth, we use the notation “top 1-5%” to denote
14:524:41265:16:17:72:540:455:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:inventors who are in the top 5% excluding the top 1%, and, similarly the top 5-10% and top 10-25%
14:525:41362:17:16:72:540:438:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:to respectively denote inventors in the top 10% excluding the top 5%, and in the top 25%, excluding
14:526:41461:16:16:72:540:422:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:the top 10%.  Whenever we write “below top 25%” we refer to the inventors who have been or will
14:527:41556:16:32:72:442:406:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:be in the top 25% during their lifetime, but are not currently in the top 25%.
14:528:41634:32:23:72:408:374:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:C:2.4    Making use of the Inventor and Top Tax Rate Data
14:529:41689:23:17:72:540:351:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:There are three main challenges when studying migration: Proxying for the counterfactual earnings
14:530:41786:17:16:72:540:334:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:in each potential destination, measuring the counterfactual tax rate, and finding exogenous variation
14:531:41887:16:21:72:358:318:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:in the tax rate.  Accordingly, we take a three step approach.
14:532:41948:21:17:72:540:297:11:g_d0_f14:11:g_d0_f3:B:Step 1: Proxying for counterfactual earnings.Our model highlighted that migration decisions
14:533:42039:17:16:72:540:280:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:should conceptually depend on the income an inventor expects to earn in each potential destination,
14:534:42138:16:17:72:311:264:11:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f5:B:which is a counterfactual, unobservable variable.21
14:535:42189:17:16:88:539:247:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:Fortunately,  the patent data gives us a rich set of measures that can proxy for an inventor’s
14:536:42283:16:16:72:540:231:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:counterfactual earnings.  Among them are the previously described quality measures,q1−q4, in
14:537:42375:16:17:71:539:215:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:formulas (1)-(4).  Patent quality to date is a composite, dynamic statistic that takes into account an
14:538:42477:17:16:71:539:198:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:inventor’s past achievements.  In that sense, it is a measure of inventor ability or earnings potential,
14:539:42581:16:17:71:277:182:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:and a reflection of the inventor’s “resume.”
14:540:42625:17:16:88:539:165:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:Patent quality and citations should increase inventors’ incomes in both a direct and an indirect
14:541:42721:16:15:71:539:149:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:way.  First, there are direct rewards and bonuses for specific innovations, driven potentially by legal
14:542:42824:15:14:80:539:134:6:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f7:F:19The other countries each account from 1.16% to 8.85% of patents.  Furthermore, the mean number of patents per
14:543:42935:14:7:72:435:120:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:F:inventor in the U.S., Japan and the rest of the countries is, respectively, 3.95, 4.7 and 3.3.
14:544:43029:7:15:80:539:113:6:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f7:F:20As  a  check,  we  also  defined  the  reference  distribution  and  ranking  separately  for  each  country,  instead  of  by
14:545:43157:15:7:72:360:98:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:F:region, and the results, available on demand, were virtually unchanged.
14:546:43228:7:15:80:539:91:6:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f7:F:21Grogger  and  Hanson  (2015)  show  that  high  ability  immigrants  are  more  likely  to  stay  where  there  is  a  high
14:547:43353:15:0:72:440:76:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:F:premium for high skill workers.  Hence, proxying well for the counterfactual wage is crucial.
15:548:43500:0:16:72:540:701:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:or contractual arrangements, such as “fair share” agreements in many countries.22These rewards
15:549:43594:16:17:72:540:685:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:depend on the value of the patent to the company, and patent citations are a clear marker for the
15:550:43691:17:18:72:377:668:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:economic value of patents (Trajtenberg,1990;Hall et al.,2001).
15:551:43753:18:16:88:539:650:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:Second, and most relevant for our purposes, there can be indirect compensation for an inventor’s
15:552:43849:16:17:71:539:634:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:ability. An employer could pay a higher salary or promote star innovators, with a stellar track record
15:553:43951:17:16:71:539:617:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:of patent quality,  in order to both attract and retain crucial talent with the best patenting and
15:554:44049:16:17:71:539:601:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:innovation ability (Chesbrough,2006).23For a lot of companies, patent licensing is also a major
15:555:44144:17:16:72:540:584:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:source of revenues, justifying the need to hire the best innovators.  For instance, IBM collects more
15:556:44245:16:17:72:540:568:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:than $1 billion in licensing revenues (Ryder and Madhavan,2014).  The importance of “stars,” who
15:557:44341:17:16:72:540:551:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:play a crucial role in the formation or transformation of many industries, has been emphasized by
15:558:44438:16:16:72:539:535:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:Zucker and Darby(2014).  Note that we are not just trying to measure the income flow from any
15:559:44531:16:17:72:540:519:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:given patent but rather to proxy for an inventor’s full earnings using quality measures based on his
15:560:44631:17:28:72:110:502:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:patents.
15:561:44639:28:17:72:539:474:11:g_d0_f14:11:g_d0_f3:B:Link  between  income  and  citations:  Whether  it  arises  from  the  direct  or  indirect  channel,
15:562:44741:17:16:72:540:457:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:there  appears  to  be  a  strong  link  between  the  value  and  quality  of  patents  and  the  inventor’s
15:563:44850:16:16:72:540:441:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:income.  The distribution of rewards for patents seems to be highly skewed towards high quality
15:564:44945:16:17:72:539:425:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:inventors.Toivanen and V ̈a ̈an ̈anen(2012) find that Finnish inventors receive a temporary reward
15:565:45043:17:16:71:539:408:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:equal to 3% of earnings for any patent grant.  This hides important heterogeneities based on patent
15:566:45142:16:17:71:539:392:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:quality:  moderately cited patents (with 20 to 30 citations) generate a premium of around 20% in
15:567:45238:17:16:71:539:375:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:annual earnings, while highly cited patents receive an earnings premium of 30% three years after
15:568:45334:16:17:71:540:359:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:the grant.Harhoff and Hoisl(2007) use data for Germany, where the employer has the right to
15:569:45425:17:16:71:539:342:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:claim the invention and, if he does, needs to reasonably compensate the employee in proportion to
15:570:45522:16:17:71:539:326:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:the value of the invention.  They also find that the share of the salary received as a compensation
15:571:45621:17:16:71:539:309:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:for an invention is highly skewed with a few top inventions doubling the inventor’s salary.  Top 5%
15:572:45720:16:16:71:539:293:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:inventors receive a 20-50% increase in their salary per invention.  Similarly, as a compensation for
15:573:45820:16:17:71:539:277:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:all inventions, the top inventors’ salaries can be multiplied by a factor of 5.Giuriet al.(2007)find
15:574:45920:17:16:71:539:260:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:in the PatVal European inventors survey that 42% of inventors receive a monetary award for their
15:575:46016:16:17:71:539:244:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:patents, and that for 4% of the respondents, these monetary rewards are permanent.  In Swedish
15:576:46110:17:16:71:539:227:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:administrative data, numbers provided to us by Olof Ejermo show that the most cited inventors
15:577:46203:16:17:71:539:211:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:earn 60% more than the less cited ones.Bellet al.(2015)find using administrative data covering
15:578:46297:17:16:71:539:194:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:the population of patent applicants in the U.S. that the distribution of income is highly skewed
15:579:46393:16:16:71:539:178:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:towards  superstar inventors with  many  citations.  In their  data,  the  mean income at  ages 40-50
15:580:46494:16:17:71:539:162:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:is close to $700,000 for inventors with 300 citations, and around $350,000 for inventors with 100
15:581:46591:17:22:71:115:145:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:citations.
15:582:46601:22:14:80:539:123:6:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f7:F:22From our own calculations and reading of the legal rules, 14% of patents in our data come from legislations where
15:583:46716:14:11:72:540:109:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:F:by law the employer owns the patent, 30% come from legislations where the employee owns the patents, and the rest
15:584:46829:11:7:72:401:98:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:F:come from legislations where ownership is determined by contractual agreements.
15:585:46908:7:15:80:539:91:6:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f7:F:23Chesbrough (2006) states that “R&D managers often use the number of patents generated (...)  as a metric to
15:586:47017:15:0:72:305:76:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:F:judge the productivity of (...)  [a] person or organization.”
16:587:47114:0:16:88:539:701:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:As described in detail in Section5.1, we will allow the ability of the inventor to be rewarded
16:588:47208:16:17:72:540:685:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:differently in different countries and we will introduce ability and country specific trends in com-
16:589:47308:17:16:72:540:668:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:pensation.   Additional  characteristics  used  to  control  for  the  counterfactual  wage  are  described
16:590:47415:16:16:72:540:652:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:there as well (such as quality measures,  technological field,  goodness of fit with the destination,
16:591:47516:16:24:72:425:636:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:tenure/experience, ability-technological-field-country-specific trends, etc.).
16:592:47594:24:16:72:540:612:11:g_d0_f14:11:g_d0_f3:B:Step 2:  Using the effective top marginal tax rate.We use the effective top marginal tax
16:593:47682:16:16:72:540:596:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:rate as our tax measure.24The estimate obtained is not necessarily interpretable as “the migration
16:594:47780:16:17:72:540:580:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:elasticity to net-of-tax income” for several reasons.  First, the average tax rate is not equal to the
16:595:47882:17:16:72:540:563:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:marginal tax rate because the tax system is not linear.  Nevertheless,  the top marginal tax rate
16:596:47979:16:17:72:539:547:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:is likely a good approximation to the average tax rate for top earners.25In addition, conditional
16:597:48076:17:16:72:540:530:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:on being in the top tax bracket, the top tax rate is exogenous to earnings, unlike the average tax
16:598:48174:16:17:72:539:514:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:rate.  The estimate is also interestingper sesince the top marginal tax rate can also be viewed as
16:599:48272:17:16:72:148:497:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:a “success tax.”
16:600:48288:16:17:88:539:481:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:Second, the estimated response will combine firm and worker responses (more on this in Section
16:601:48382:17:16:72:540:464:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:5.4) and will be a function of institutional features (e.g., visa regulations, as illustrated starkly for
16:602:48487:16:17:72:540:448:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:the  case  of  Russian  inventors  in  Section4.1),  both  of  which  prevent  an  easy  mapping  from  the
16:603:48594:17:16:72:303:431:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:reduced form estimates to behavioral primitives.
16:604:48642:16:17:88:539:415:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:Finally, there are other taxes which may influence migration decision, such as corporate taxes
16:605:48736:17:16:72:540:398:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:or  capital  gains  taxes.   However,  we  limit  the  sample  to  inventors  who  are  employees  and  who
16:606:48843:16:17:72:540:382:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:hence  receive  the  bulk  of  their  income  as  ordinary  personal  income.   These  inventors  innovate
16:607:48949:17:16:72:540:365:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:within companies and, typically, their employers are the owners of the patents obtained.  To a first
16:608:49049:16:17:72:540:349:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:order, this allows us to abstract from other forms of taxation such as capital taxation, corporate
16:609:49147:17:16:72:540:332:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:taxation, or royalties’ taxation, and instead focus on personal income taxation.  We do control for
16:610:49246:16:16:72:539:316:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:capital gains and corporate taxes in Appendix TableA14and check our results on the full sample,
16:611:49341:16:17:72:306:300:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:including non-employees in Appendix TableA16.
16:612:49386:17:17:88:539:283:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:There  are  certainly  some  complications  with  foreign  tax  rules  and  regimes  across  different
16:613:49488:17:16:71:539:266:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:countries,  which we are not able to account for given our data.  For instance,  an inventor living
16:614:49587:16:16:71:539:250:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:temporarily in the UK but domiciled abroad can choose to some extent how to be taxed on his
16:615:49678:16:17:71:539:234:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:income  earned  abroad  (on  an  “arising  basis”  or  on  a  “remittance  basis”).   Depending  on  the
16:616:49782:17:16:71:539:217:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:inventor’s (unobservable) legal arrangements and future plans, this might lead to somewhat different
16:617:49882:16:17:71:539:201:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:effective marginal tax rates.  In the analysis, we assume that, to a first order, the inventor pays the
16:618:49985:17:17:71:539:184:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:taxes of the country he physically resides in.  The exception is for U.S. inventors who are taxed on
16:619:50085:17:14:80:539:167:6:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f7:F:24One way to interpret the obtained elasticity is as a reduced form estimate, where the top marginal tax rate can
16:620:50198:14:11:72:540:153:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:F:act like an instrument for the top average tax rate.  The implicit “first-stage” is indeed significant:  from our own
16:621:50315:11:11:72:540:142:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:F:computations,  we  see  that  changes  in  the  top  marginal  tax  rate  are  very  strongly  correlated  with  changes  in  the
16:622:50444:11:8:72:308:131:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:F:average tax rate on the top 1% of the income distribution.
16:623:50502:8:14:80:539:123:6:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f7:F:25Reassuringly, Kleven, Landais, and Saez (2013) show that the elasticities obtained for football players using the
16:624:50617:14:11:72:540:109:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:F:marginal top tax rate versus actual average tax rates are very similar.  This hinges on the fact that those football
16:625:50733:11:11:72:540:98:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:F:players  considered  are  well  above  the  top  tax  bracket  in  terms  of  earnings.   In  our  data  we  find  a  very  strong
16:626:50863:11:11:72:540:87:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:F:correlation between the average tax rate on top earners (evaluated using the tax codes for different countries) and
16:627:50978:11:0:72:177:76:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:F:the top marginal tax rate.
17:628:51058:0:16:72:194:701:11:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f5:B:their worldwide income.26
17:629:51083:16:17:88:539:685:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:The effective top marginal tax rate is computed including all relevant taxes on labor income:
17:630:51176:17:16:72:540:668:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:the  individual  local,  state,  and  national  tax  rates,  the  uncapped  payroll  taxes,  and  value-added
17:631:51285:16:17:72:539:652:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:taxes.  These series come fromPiketty,  Saez,  and Stantcheva (2014).  For U.S. citizens,  who are
17:632:51383:17:16:72:540:635:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:taxed on worldwide income, a special top tax rate is computed for each possible location choice,
17:633:51479:16:17:72:540:619:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:taking into account the Foreign Tax Credit formula.27We drop people in the years in which they
17:634:51573:17:16:72:540:602:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:are observed in different countries within the same year, as it is not clear what tax rate their yearly
17:635:51676:16:23:72:257:586:11:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f5:B:income was subject to in those years.28
17:636:51715:23:17:72:540:563:11:g_d0_f14:11:g_d0_f3:B:Step  3:  Identification  using  different  quality  inventors.As  Appendix  FigureA1shows,
17:637:51806:17:16:72:540:546:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:there have been many,  both small and large,  top tax rate changes in our sample.  The simplest
17:638:51901:16:16:72:540:530:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:identification  strategy  exploits  these  variations  across  countries  and  time  (i.e.,  country-by-year
17:639:52009:16:17:72:540:514:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:variation) in top marginal tax rates.  In this case, it is still important to control for country fixed
17:640:52112:17:16:72:540:497:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:effects,  year  fixed  effects,  as  well  as  for  country  specific  linear  trends  to  filter  out  longer-term
17:641:52227:16:17:72:540:481:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:country-specific evolutions in innovation, incomes, and migration.  We view this strategy only as
17:642:52324:17:16:72:540:464:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:a first pass,  as there may be other factors correlated with top marginal tax rates which vary at
17:643:52421:16:17:72:540:448:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:the same time in a given country, such as the business friendliness of the environment or research
17:644:52519:17:16:72:540:431:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:stimulating policies.  If there are general equilibrium effects of top taxes at the country-year level,
17:645:52622:16:17:72:386:415:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:these will also be loaded on the estimated coefficient of top taxes.
17:646:52690:17:16:88:539:398:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:Our main and preferred identification instead filters out all variation at the country-year level
17:647:52787:16:17:72:540:382:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:and exploits the differential impact of changes in the top marginal tax rate on the top superstar
17:648:52884:17:16:72:540:365:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:inventors  and  slightly  lower  quality  inventors.   The  idea  is  that  the  top  1%  inventors  and  those
17:649:52995:16:17:72:540:349:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:of slightly lower qualities should be subject to the same country-year level policies and economic
17:650:53093:17:16:72:540:332:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:effects because they are all very high quality inventors.  However, only inventors who are actually
17:651:53192:16:16:72:540:316:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:in the top bracket are directly affected by the changes in top tax rates.  The evidence presented
17:652:53289:16:17:72:540:300:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:below  suggests  that  top  1%  superstar  inventors  are  well  in  the  top  tax  bracket.   While  the  top
17:653:53399:17:16:72:540:283:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:1-5% are still very likely to be in the top bracket, the likelihood of being in the top tax bracket
17:654:53498:16:17:72:540:267:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:declines sharply as we move down through the top 5-10% to the top 10-25% or the below top 25%
17:655:53591:17:16:72:138:250:11:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f5:B:of inventors.29
17:656:53606:16:17:88:539:234:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:Conceptually, this main identification strategy is akin to a “fuzzy regression discontinuity de-
17:657:53702:17:16:72:540:217:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:sign” where the quality ranking generates a fuzzy threshold above which inventors are “treated” by
17:658:53800:16:17:72:540:201:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:the top tax rate changes.  The lower quality, top 5-10%, top 10-25%, or below the top 25% groups
17:659:53896:17:17:72:540:184:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:serve as control groups for the top 1%.  The top 1-5% is treated as a buffer group, and not as a
17:660:53992:17:14:80:539:167:6:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f7:F:26Incidentally, in Section 6.3, we consider long-term mobility, which potentially allows a clearer equivalence between
17:661:54110:14:11:72:540:153:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:F:geographical location and tax residency, since it is harder to shift income abroad when residing long-term in a different
17:662:54231:11:8:72:107:142:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:F:location.
17:663:54240:8:14:80:539:134:6:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f7:F:27Given the Foreign Tax Credit rules for U.S. citizens, we set the tax rate for U.S. citizen abroad equal to the U.S.
17:664:54357:14:11:72:540:120:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:F:tax if and only if the foreign tax rate is smaller than the U.S. tax rate:  this was frequently the case before 1985 for
17:665:54477:11:7:72:369:109:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:F:the 8 countries under consideration, but not the case anymore after 1985.
17:666:54550:7:11:80:343:102:6:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f7:A:28Less than 0.2% of the observations are dropped for this reason.
17:667:54615:11:15:80:540:91:6:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f7:F:29As explained in Section5.1, the “below top 25%” group refers to inventors who have been or will be in the top
17:668:54726:15:0:72:427:76:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:F:25% at some point during their life in the sample, but are not currently in the top 25%.
18:669:54850:0:16:72:461:701:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:good control group, since inventors in this group are too likely to also be treated.
18:670:54934:16:17:88:539:685:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:The discontinuity is fuzzy because tax brackets differ across countries and because we do not
18:671:55027:17:16:72:540:668:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:know counterfactual income and have to instead use quality rankings.  We hence establish in two
18:672:55122:16:17:72:540:652:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:steps, by reference to the literature, that, first, quality is highly positively related to income and
18:673:55224:17:16:72:540:635:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:that, second, inventor’s income distributions are such that the top income inventors are in the top
18:674:55323:16:17:72:540:619:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:bracket (this is done further below).  A useful way to think about this is that the quality groups
18:675:55421:17:16:72:400:602:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:capture the propensity to be “treated” by the top marginal tax rate.
18:676:55489:16:17:88:539:586:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:When choosing the control group, there is a typical trade-off between maximizing comparability
18:677:55583:17:16:72:540:569:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:(i.e., choosing a group very close in quality e.g., the top 5-10%) and minimizing the control group’s
18:678:55684:16:17:72:540:553:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:propensity of being treated (i.e., choosing a lower quality group such as the below top 25%).  For
18:679:55782:17:16:72:540:536:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:instance,  the  top  1%  (the  treatment  group)  and  the  top  5-10%  are  likely  extremely  comparable
18:680:55888:16:16:72:540:520:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:groups  along  all  dimensions.   However,  the  top  5-10%  may  still  include  quite  a  few  “treated”
18:681:55994:16:17:72:540:504:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:inventors  in  the  top  bracket.   In  addition,  inventors  in  the  top  5-10%  may  still  feel  the  indirect
18:682:56108:17:16:72:540:487:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:motivational effect of the “success tax.”  As a result, we may underestimate the “treatment” effect
18:683:56207:16:17:72:540:471:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:of the top tax rate if comparing only to the top 5-10% group.  We therefore find it useful to show
18:684:56305:17:16:72:540:454:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:the estimated coefficients for all inventor groups and to compute the elasticities for different choices
18:685:56409:16:17:72:540:438:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:of control group.  We hence include in the regression the full set of interactions of the retention rate
18:686:56513:17:16:72:540:421:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:with indicator variables for being in the top 1%, the top 1-5%, the top 5-10%, the top 10-25%, and
18:687:56611:16:16:72:540:405:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:the below top 25%.  To reiterate, this identification allows us to include country-year fixed effects
18:688:56712:16:17:72:482:389:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:in the estimation in order to filter out other contemporaneous changes in the country.
18:689:56798:17:17:88:539:372:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:Our strategy is similar in spirit to that in other studies which exploit the differential impact
18:690:56894:17:16:72:540:355:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:of tax changes across income tax brackets, using lower income brackets as control groups for top
18:691:56990:16:16:72:539:339:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:brackets (Eissa,1995), or across households with different non-labor income and family size (Eissa
18:692:57088:16:17:72:539:323:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:and  Hoynes,2006).   We  are  most  closely  inspired  by  a  strategy  that  captures  the  differential
18:693:57193:17:16:72:540:306:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:propensities of being “treated,” as inHoynes and Schanzenbach(2009) orHoynes and Schanzenbach
18:694:57286:16:17:72:540:290:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:(2012) who multiply Food Stamp program introduction by propensity to participate (proxied by
18:695:57378:17:16:72:540:273:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:group-level food stamp participation):  in our case, we interact the top tax rate with the inventor’s
18:696:57479:16:17:72:540:257:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:quality  ranking  (which  proxies  the  propensity  of  being  in  the  top  bracket).   Note  that  we  are
18:697:57587:17:16:72:540:240:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:unable to compute an actual propensity to be treated as inHoynes and Schanzenbach(2009).  The
18:698:57680:16:16:72:540:224:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:problem for doing this is bigger than just the fact that we do not have data on inventor income
18:699:57775:16:17:72:539:208:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:distributions conditional on quality: we do not knowcounterfactualincome (and there is no dataset
18:700:57872:17:16:72:540:191:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:that contains it) and so we would not be able to know the inventor’s actual propensity to be treated
18:701:57972:16:17:72:312:175:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:in each potential destination country in each year.
18:702:58023:17:16:88:539:158:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:For this identification, we may worry that changes in top tax rates are correlated with changes
18:703:58118:16:17:72:540:142:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:in  the  average  tax  rate  of  the  slightly  lower  quality  groups.   Historically,  this  does  not  seem  to
18:704:58232:17:16:72:540:125:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:have been the case in our setting.  There have overall been 218 top tax rate changes in our sample.
18:705:58331:16:17:72:540:109:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:For  only  7  of  these  have  the  top  marginal  tax  rate  and  the  tax  rate  in  the  bracket  below  both
18:706:58443:17:16:72:540:92:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:increased, and for only 14 have they both decreased.  Note here that we would mostly be worried
18:707:58538:16:0:72:540:76:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:about situations in which the top marginal tax rate and the rate in the bracket below would move
19:708:58688:0:16:72:540:701:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:in the opposite direction, which is the only case that would lead us to overestimate the effect of
19:709:58786:16:25:72:540:685:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:the top MTR with this identification strategy.  Fortunately, this has never occurred in our sample.
19:710:58885:25:17:72:539:660:11:g_d0_f14:11:g_d0_f3:B:Inventors’ income distributions:Because of our identification strategy, we need to check that
19:711:58978:17:16:72:540:643:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:the top quality inventors are in the top income tax bracket, while the propensity of being in the
19:712:59075:16:17:72:540:627:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:top bracket declines for lower quality inventors.  This is done in two steps.  First,  recall that we
19:713:59176:17:16:72:540:610:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:established a very significant positive link between citations and income above.  We now focus on
19:714:59273:16:16:72:540:594:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:the income distribution of inventors – keeping this link in mind– to show which percentiles of the
19:715:59371:16:18:72:451:578:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:inventors’ income distribution are in the top bracket and which ones are below.
19:716:59450:18:16:88:539:560:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:Using data from the 2003 National Survey of College Graduates public-use microdata from the
19:717:59541:16:17:72:540:544:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:NSF (NSF, 2003),  Figure2 shows that 44% of inventors are in the top 10% of the U.S. income
19:718:59632:17:16:71:539:527:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:distribution,  18% are in the top 5%,  and 1% are in the top 1% of the U.S. income distribution.
19:719:59728:16:16:71:540:511:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:A more reliable source is the administrative data used inBell et al.(2014) which shows that, in
19:720:59823:16:17:71:539:495:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:terms  of  income,  the  top  1%  inventor  earns  $1.6  million  and  the  top  5%  earns  $500,000.   The
19:721:59930:17:16:71:539:478:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:median inventor earns $114,000 and the mean inventor earns $192,000.  The top 1% highest quality
19:722:60026:16:17:71:539:462:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:inventors  are  hence  quite  likely  to  be  very  high  up  in  the  income  distribution.   The  top  1-5%
19:723:60135:17:16:71:539:445:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:inventors by quality are still very high up and have a large propensity of being in the top bracket.
19:724:60235:16:22:71:312:429:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:The top 5-10% by quality have a lower propensity.
19:725:60284:22:206:91:516:407:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f8:A:Figure 2: Distribution of Inventor Earnings in the NSF Survey 2003
19:726:60365:206:9:210:472:201:72:Helvetica:72:Helvetica:?:100000200000300000400000500000

19:731:60591:13:14:72:540:127:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:F:The earnings represented are those of the college graduates with at least one patent and who report being currently
19:732:60706:14:21:72:214:113:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:F:employed.  The sample size is 3142.
19:733:60741:21:16:88:540:92:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:Turning to European countries and Japan, Figure3 uses inventor survey data, and plots the
19:734:60830:16:0:72:540:76:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:income distribution relative to the top bracket.  It highlights that the top 1% of inventors in terms
20:735:60967:0:16:72:540:701:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:of  income  are  clearly  comfortably  in  the  top  income  tax  brackets,  and  the  top  1-5%  or  the  top
20:736:61077:16:17:72:540:685:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:5-10% are still quite likely to be in the top tax bracket.  Below the top 10% the propensity to be
20:737:61175:17:43:72:215:668:11:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f5:B:treated seems sharply lower.30
20:738:61205:43:30:72:244:625:14:g_d0_f2:14:g_d0_f2:C:3    Stylized Macro Facts
20:739:61230:30:16:72:540:595:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:We start by providing some stylized macroeconomic facts about the correlations between top re-
20:740:61324:16:17:72:540:579:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:tention rates and migration at the country-year level.  This evidence is suggestive that, even at an
20:741:61424:17:16:72:540:562:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:aggregate level, there is a significant correlation between inventor migration and top taxes, which
20:742:61523:16:38:72:265:546:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:is concentrated on top quality inventors.
20:743:61564:38:25:72:335:508:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:C:3.1    Macro correlations in the inventor data
20:744:61610:25:17:72:540:483:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:Figure 4 considers the relation between migration and top tax rates where each dot represents one
20:745:61707:17:16:72:540:466:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:country in a given year.  In all panels, the outcome variable is adjusted for a country’s GDP, patent
20:746:61808:16:17:72:540:450:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:stock,  country fixed effects and year fixed effects,  thus filtering out time invariant cross-country
20:747:61910:17:17:72:125:433:11:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f5:B:variation.31
20:748:61922:17:16:88:539:416:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:Panel A focuses on the fraction of domestic inventors who remain in their home country.  Figure
20:749:62017:16:17:72:540:400:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:4a shows that the decision to remain in the home country is significantly affected by top tax rates,
20:750:62117:17:16:72:540:383:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:with  an  elasticity  of  0.08.   On  the  other  hand,  there  is  no  significant  relation  between  top  tax
20:751:62229:16:17:72:539:367:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:rates and the fraction of low quality inventors in Figure4bas should be expected given that these
20:752:62326:17:16:72:540:350:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:inventors are not in the top tax bracket.  Panel B turns to the number of foreign inventors as a
20:753:62422:16:17:72:540:334:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:fraction  of  all  inventors  in  a  country.   Figure4cagain  shows  that  top  quality  foreigners  exhibit
20:754:62531:17:16:72:539:317:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:a  significant  elasticity  of  0.47,  while  the  elasticity  of  low  quality  foreigners  in  Figure4dis  not
20:755:62643:16:38:72:401:301:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:significant.  Table2 columns (1) and (2) summarize these elasticities.
20:756:62713:38:25:72:293:263:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:C:3.2    Cross-check using the PCT data
20:757:62750:25:17:72:540:238:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:As  an  additional  piece  of  macro  evidence  we  use  the  alternative  data  source  from  patents  filed
20:758:62859:17:17:72:408:221:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:under the Patent Cooperation Treaty (PCT), described in Section2.3.
20:759:62926:17:17:88:540:204:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:Figure5aplots  the  average  share  of  domestic  inventors  in  each  country  against  the  average
20:760:63027:17:20:72:540:187:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:top retention rate over the period 1980-2004.  There is a significantly positive relationship, with an
20:761:63129:20:14:80:539:167:6:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f7:F:30In Swedish administrative data matched to the patent data, even more lower quality inventors seem to be treated.
20:762:63243:14:11:72:540:153:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:F:We can see that in 2000, the top 10% inventor earns SEK 648,400, the top 5% inventor earns SEK 775300 and the
20:763:63352:11:11:72:540:142:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:F:top 1% earns close to 2 times more at SEK 1,171,000.  The median inventor earns SEK 355,200.  The top tax bracket
20:764:63465:11:11:72:540:131:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:F:threshold  in  that  year  was  SEK  374,000.   Olof  Ejermo  kindly  provided  us  with  these  numbers  from  the  Swedish
20:765:63589:11:7:72:170:120:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:F:administrative tax data.
20:766:63613:7:15:80:540:113:6:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f7:F:31In  these  partial  residual  plots,  for  any  outcomeYwe  regress  log(Y)  on  country  GDP,  patent  stock,  country
20:767:63734:15:11:72:540:98:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:F:fixed effects, year fixed effects, and the top log retention rate, clustered at the country level.  We then construct the
20:768:63855:11:11:72:540:87:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:F:adjusted outcome as log(Y) from which we subtract all covariates (except the log retention rate) times their estimated
20:769:63973:11:0:71:117:76:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:F:coefficients.

24:868:69909:0:29:72:250:701:14:g_d0_f2:14:g_d0_f2:C:4    Country Case Studies
24:869:69934:29:16:72:540:672:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:We now turn to specific country case studies which exploit large historic breaks due to migration
24:870:70031:16:39:72:143:656:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:or tax reforms.
24:871:70046:39:26:72:452:617:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:C:4.1    Russian inventors’ migration and the Soviet Union collapse
24:872:70111:26:16:72:540:591:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:Our first case study concerns Russian inventors, a group of inventors whose migration was essentially
24:873:70212:16:18:72:351:575:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:impossible before the collapse of the Soviet Union in 1991.
24:874:70271:18:16:88:539:557:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:We  use  two  sources  of  data,  starting  with  the  PCT  data  which  has  actual  nationality  infor-
24:875:70376:16:17:72:539:541:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:mation.   As  a  first  pass,  Figure6,  plots  the  average  number  of  Russian  immigrants  in  different
24:876:70484:17:16:72:540:524:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:countries as a function of the average top retention rate before and after the collapse of the Soviet
24:877:70585:16:16:72:539:508:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:Union.  Before 1991 (in panel6a), the relationship is flat at zero, since Russian nationals were not
24:878:70685:16:17:72:540:492:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:able to react to tax differentials because of stark migration restrictions.  By contrast, after 1991 (in
24:879:70789:17:16:72:540:475:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:panel6b), a significantly negative relationship between Russian inventors and top tax rates rates
24:880:70886:16:22:72:112:459:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:appears.

24:904:71252:7:38:398:458:244:35:Helvetica:35:g_d0_f30:?:Top marginal tax rate τ
24:905:71275:38:11:72:540:206:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:F:Note:  Based  on  the  PCT  data  that  contains  nationality  information.   Each  dot  represents  one  country’s  average
24:906:71399:11:10:72:540:195:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:F:outcome over the period.  AU= Australia,  AT=Austria,  BE=Belgium,  DK=Denmark,  UK=England,  FR=France,

24:908:71613:11:11:72:540:174:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:F:ES=Spain, SE=Sweden, CH=Switzerland.  Panel (a) is the pre-Soviet Union collapse period (1977-1991) and panel
24:909:71722:11:11:72:540:163:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:F:(b) is the post-Soviet union collapse period (1992-2003). The elasticities reported (with standard errors in parenthesis)
24:910:71843:11:11:72:539:152:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:F:come from an OLS regression of the log outcome on log(1−τ) whereτis the top marginal tax rate on the x-axis (for
24:911:71955:11:11:71:539:141:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:F:the pre-period, the number of Russian inventors is zero so we use the level of the outcome in the regressions).  When
24:912:72072:11:21:71:522:130:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:F:migration was allowed post 1991, a negative correlation between Russian migration and top tax rates appeared.
24:913:72181:21:17:88:539:109:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:Next we move beyond correlations and exploit our main identification strategy, which consists
24:914:72274:17:16:71:539:92:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:in comparing the effects of the top tax rate on top quality relative to lower quality inventors.  For
24:915:72375:16:0:71:539:76:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:this, we turn to our main DID, which has detailed quality measures for inventors.  We combine the
25:916:72526:0:16:72:539:701:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:DID with the ethnicity data byKerr(2008), to circumvent the problem of the lack of nationality
25:917:72620:16:17:71:539:685:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:information.Kerr(2008) uses an ethnic names database to assign inventors’ ethnicities, so we know
25:918:72717:17:16:71:539:668:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:which inventors have Russian ethnicity.  Hence, there are of course inventors of Russian ethnicity
25:919:72815:16:16:71:460:652:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:abroad even before 1991 (unlike for the pure nationality measure from the PCT).
25:920:72894:16:17:88:539:636:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:We can now exploit the differential impact of the top tax rate on higher versus lower quality
25:921:72987:17:16:71:539:619:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:inventors.   Low  quality  Russian  inventors  can  here  serve  as  a  control  group  that  shares  similar
25:922:73096:16:17:71:539:603:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:affinities with each potential destination country as higher quality inventors, and would hence filter
25:923:73198:17:16:71:539:586:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:out reasons unrelated to taxes (but potentially correlated with them) for which Russian inventors
25:924:73295:16:17:71:539:570:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:may want to move to specific countries.  Low quality Russian inventors,  however,  should not be
25:925:73391:17:16:71:231:553:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:directly affected by top tax rates.
25:926:73426:16:17:88:540:537:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:In Figures7aand7b, we plot the ratio of foreign top 1% inventors over bottom 50% inventors as
25:927:73519:17:16:71:539:520:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:a function of the top tax rate, pre and post 1991.  Each dot represents a country-year observation.
25:928:73618:16:16:71:539:504:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:We can see the clear differential effect of the top tax rate on top quality Russian inventors relative to
25:929:73723:16:17:71:539:488:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:low quality Russian inventors.  Pre-1991 there is a slightly positive (insignificant) relation between
25:930:73825:17:16:71:539:471:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:the relative number of foreigners in the top 1% versus the bottom 50% and top tax rates, but this
25:931:73922:16:22:71:400:455:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:relation becomes negative and significant post-Soviet Union collapse.
25:932:73991:22:25:85:527:433:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f8:A:Figure 7: Top quality versus low quality Russian inventors’ migration
25:933:74060:25:162:92:288:408:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:?:(a) Top 1% over Bottom 50% inventors pre-1991

25:937:74331:45:11:72:540:201:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:F:Note:  Based on DID, combined with ethnicity data from Kerr (2008).  Kerr (2008) uses an algorithm that identifies
25:938:74445:11:11:72:540:190:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:F:Russian ethnicity inventors.  The figures represent the ratio of top 1% superstar Russian inventors relative to the
25:939:74560:11:11:72:540:179:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:F:bottom 50% low quality Russian inventors.  Each dot represents a country-year observation.  Before 1991 there is
25:940:74672:11:11:72:540:168:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:F:some ethnic Russian diaspora abroad, which is not significantly correlated with top tax rates (coefficient of 0.105,
25:941:74788:11:11:72:540:157:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:F:with standard error 0.09).  Post Soviet Union collapse, there is a significant negative correlation between superstar
25:942:74905:11:11:72:540:146:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:F:top 1% Russian inventors relative to lower quality Russian inventors and top tax rates (the coefficient is -0.111, with
25:943:75024:11:11:72:540:135:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:F:standard error 0.028).  Analogous regressions with additional controls for log GDP per capita, log number of patents
25:944:75140:11:11:72:540:124:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:F:and  country  and  year  fixed  effects  produces  coefficients  for  pre-1991  of  -0.09,  with  standard  error  0.075,  and  for
25:945:75271:11:21:72:260:113:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:F:post-1991 of -0.199, with standard error 0.092.
25:946:75318:21:16:88:539:92:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:Table 3 shows the elasticity estimates for inventors of different quality. It confirms that while top
25:947:75419:16:0:72:540:76:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:1% superstar inventors’ migration was unsurprisingly not related to top tax rates before the collapse
26:948:75556:0:16:72:540:701:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:of the Soviet Union, there is a very significant elasticity to top tax rates post 1991.  The same effect,
26:949:75661:16:17:72:540:685:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:but much weaker, is visible for top 1-50% inventors.  The elasticity of the top 1% superstar Russian
26:950:75761:17:21:72:532:668:11:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f5:B:inventors matches quite closely the elasticity of foreigners in the micro estimation in Section5.32
26:951:75860:21:18:103:503:647:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f8:C:Table 3: Elasticity of Russian inventors to top retention rates

26:965:76811:37:24:72:315:443:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:C:4.2    United States Tax Reform Act 1986
26:966:76851:24:16:72:540:419:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:Next,  to  dig  deeper  into  the  identification  of  the  effects  of  top  tax  rates,  we  exploit  the  quasi-
26:967:76966:16:17:72:540:403:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:experimental variation provided by two large tax reforms:  the U.S. Tax Reform Act of 1986 and
26:968:77060:17:16:72:332:386:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:Denmark’s 1992 preferential tax scheme for foreigners.
26:969:77114:16:16:88:539:370:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:To study the effects of these reforms on inventor migration, we use the synthetic control method
26:970:77210:16:17:72:539:354:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:byAbadie et al.(2010). It consists in building a synthetic control country that is a weighted average
26:971:77311:17:16:72:540:337:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:of  other  countries  in  the  sample.   The  weights  are  chosen  to  minimize  the  pre-reform  distance
26:972:77418:16:17:72:540:321:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:between the country under consideration (i.e., U.S. or Denmark) and the synthetic country along
26:973:77513:17:16:72:540:304:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:dimensions of interest.  The synthetic country plausibly represents what would have happened in
26:974:77608:16:17:72:417:288:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:the control country absent the reform.  AppendixD provides the details.
26:975:77679:17:16:88:539:271:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:To estimate the elasticities to top tax rates, we regress at the country-year level the log of each
26:976:77778:16:17:72:540:255:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:outcome  variable  on  the  log  retention  rate,  a  dummy  for  the  post-reform  period  and  a  dummy
26:977:77883:17:16:72:540:238:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:for country (there are two “countries” here, namely the treated country and the synthetic control
26:978:77980:16:16:72:540:222:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:country),  where the log retention rate is instrumented by the interaction of the country dummy
26:979:78075:16:17:72:243:206:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:and the post-reform period dummy.
26:980:78108:17:16:88:540:189:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:The U.S. Tax Reform Act of 1986 reduced top marginal tax rates from 50% to 28%.33The
26:981:78192:16:17:72:540:173:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:corresponding change in average tax rates was very concentrated at the top of the income distri-
26:982:78288:17:14:80:539:156:6:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f7:F:32Note  that  because  Kerr  (2008)  assigns  ethnicity  (not  nationality),  it  is  expected  to  see  some  ethnic  Russian
26:983:78414:14:11:72:540:142:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:F:inventors  abroad  in  the  Soviet  Union  era.   What  matters  here  is  how  the  elasticity  changed  in  the  post  collapse
26:984:78543:11:11:72:540:131:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:F:period.  For low bottom 50% Russian inventors, as expected, the correlation between migration and top tax rates did
26:985:78658:11:7:72:228:120:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:F:not change post-Soviet Union collapse.
26:986:78696:7:15:80:539:113:6:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f7:F:33There is still a debate about the extent to which the decrease in marginal tax rates was offset by base broadening,
26:987:78813:15:11:72:540:98:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:F:which was one of the goals of the reform.Gravelle and Hungerford(2012) argue that the tax base of the individual
26:988:78925:11:11:72:539:87:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:F:income tax was not widely broadened.Bakija and Steuerle(1991) find an overall modest increase in the tax base of
26:989:79037:11:0:72:94:76:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:F:3.8%.
27:990:79096:0:16:72:540:701:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:bution.  According to our own calculations, average tax rates decreased by a large 7.6% for the top
27:991:79195:16:17:72:540:685:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:1%, decreased by only 2% for the top 5% of inventors, and actually increased by 0.7% for the top
27:992:79291:17:16:72:223:668:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:10% of the income distribution.
27:993:79322:16:16:88:539:652:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:Figure  8  plots  the  number  of  foreign  inventors  in  the  U.S.  and  in  its  synthetic  counterpart,
27:994:79429:16:17:72:539:636:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:normalized by a base year (1986).34We again use our preferred identification (and the differential
27:995:79527:17:16:72:540:619:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:impact  of  top  tax  rates  on  inventors  of  different  qualities),  and  show  the  effects  of  this  reform
27:996:79640:16:23:72:514:603:11:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f5:B:separately for top quality (top 1%) and slightly lower quality (here, top 10-25%) inventors.35
27:997:79734:23:39:87:524:580:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f8:A:Figure 8: The 1986 Tax Reform Act and Foreign Inventors in the U.S.

27:1008:80158:13:8:393:527:383:0:Helvetica:0:Helvetica:?:U.S.Synthetic U.S.
27:1009:80176:8:41:393:454:375:0:Helvetica:0:Helvetica:?:Top tax rate differential
27:1010:80201:41:11:72:540:334:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:F:Notes:  The 1986 Tax Reform Act (implemented during the fiscal year represented by the grey vertical area), lowered
27:1011:80316:11:11:72:540:323:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:F:top tax rates in the U.S. In each panel,  the fraction of foreign inventors in the U.S. versus the fraction of foreign
27:1012:80434:11:11:72:540:312:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:F:inventors in the synthetic control country are depicted.  The weights on countries forming the synthetic country are
27:1013:80550:11:11:72:539:301:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:F:set to minimize the distance to the U.S. in the pre-reform years (see the text and Appendix Dfor details).  Panel8a
27:1014:80665:11:11:72:539:290:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:F:shows the number of top 1% foreign inventors in the U.S., while panel8bdisplays the number of top 10-25% foreigners
27:1015:80780:11:11:72:540:279:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:F:in the U.S. Both are normalized by a base year (1986).  The red line shows the top tax rate differential between the
27:1016:80896:11:11:72:540:268:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:F:U.S. and the synthetic control country (on the right axis), i.e.,τUS/τsynthetic−1.  We report the difference-in-difference
27:1017:81018:11:20:72:238:257:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:F:elasticity estimates described in the text.
27:1018:81061:20:16:88:539:237:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:Indeed, the differential effect of the top tax rate change on the foreign superstar top 1% inventors
27:1019:81161:16:17:72:540:221:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:is visible in two ways.  First, purely exploiting the logic of the synthetic control method, we can
27:1020:81260:17:16:72:540:204:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:show  that  the  number  of  foreign  top  1%  superstar  inventors  increased  drastically  relative  to  a
27:1021:81368:16:17:72:540:188:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:scenario with no reform (as proxied by the synthetic control), while this was not the case for the
27:1022:81466:17:16:72:540:171:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:lower quality top 10-25% foreign inventors.  In panel (a), the red line (on the y axis) is the top tax
27:1023:81568:16:21:72:539:155:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:differential between the U.S. and the synthetic country, defined asτUSτsynthetic−1.  While top tax rates
27:1024:81672:21:14:80:539:134:6:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f7:F:34Some normalization is necessary because the U.S. is the largest country in the data and it would not make sense
27:1025:81785:14:11:72:540:120:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:F:to try and match levels.  It would also not make sense to look at the fraction of foreigners, since the reform was not
27:1026:81903:11:7:72:453:109:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:F:preferentially targeting foreigners (unlike Denmark’s reform discussed in the next Subsection).
27:1027:81998:7:15:80:539:102:6:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f7:F:35Recall that the top 1-5% group still has a very high propensity of being treated and is hence not a good control
27:1028:82112:15:11:72:540:87:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:F:group.  The results described next naturally also hold if we consider even lower quality inventors, e.g., the below top
27:1029:82231:11:0:72:483:76:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:F:25%, etc., subject to the trade-offs involved in choosing the control group, as described in Section2.4.
28:1030:82371:0:16:72:540:701:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:were about the same in the U.S. and in the control country, they diverge sharply post reform.36The
28:1031:82469:16:17:72:540:685:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:pre-reform trends are extremely close in the U.S. and the synthetic country.  However, the series for
28:1032:82570:17:16:72:540:668:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:top 1% foreign superstar inventors diverge exactly at the time of the U.S. tax reform between the
28:1033:82667:16:16:72:540:652:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:U.S. and the synthetic control country.  When we repeat the analysis for the lower quality group
28:1034:82763:16:17:72:540:636:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:of inventors (the top 10-25%),  we do not see such an effect:  there is no break in the trend post
28:1035:82861:17:16:72:540:619:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:reform and, if anything, the U.S. series for the top 10-25% foreign inventors fall a bit relative to
28:1036:82961:16:17:72:540:603:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:the synthetic control.  Hence, the lower quality top 10-25% foreign inventors, fare similarly in the
28:1037:83061:17:16:72:540:586:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:U.S. (which decreased its top tax rates) and in the other countries (which did not decrease top tax
28:1038:83160:16:26:72:102:570:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:rates).
28:1039:83167:26:16:88:539:544:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:The second way to see the differential effect of the reform on foreign superstar top 1% inventors
28:1040:83264:16:16:72:540:528:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:is  to  directly  consider  the  structural  break  in  their  series  relative  to  that  of  foreign  top  10-25%
28:1041:83379:16:17:72:540:512:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:inventors.  Naturally, all the series for foreigners are growing due to the general growth in patents,
28:1042:83481:17:16:72:540:495:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:inventors,  and innovation over time,  but we can directly compare what happened to the growth
28:1043:83575:16:17:72:540:479:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:rates of the top 1% foreign inventors and of the top 10-25% foreign inventors after the 1986 reform.
28:1044:83675:17:16:72:540:462:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:Comparing the two solid black lines in panels (a) and (b), we see that while the top 10-25% group
28:1045:83772:16:17:72:540:446:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:was  growing  faster  before  the  reform,  it  is  the  top  1%  that  started  growing  much  more  rapidly
28:1046:83881:17:16:72:540:429:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:post reform.  More specifically, pre-reform, the top 10-25% series was growing on average at 12.7%
28:1047:83979:16:16:72:540:413:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:per year,  while the top 1% was growing at only 6.8% per year during the same period.  On the
28:1048:84072:16:17:72:540:397:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:other hand, after the reform, the top 10-25% was still growing at about the same rate (11.3% per
28:1049:84168:17:16:72:540:380:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:year), while the top 1% drastically accelerated to 16.4% per year.  As a result, the composition of
28:1050:84267:16:17:72:540:364:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:foreign inventors in the U.S. dramatically changed after the 1986 reform, and the ratio of the top
28:1051:84365:17:38:72:379:347:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:1% foreigners to the top 10-25% foreigners drastically increased.
28:1052:84430:38:25:72:241:309:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:C:4.3    Denmark’s 1992 reform
28:1053:84458:25:17:72:539:284:11:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f5:B:Next, we consider the Danish 1992 reform, studied inKleven et al.(2013) andKleven et al.(2014).37
28:1054:84555:17:16:71:539:267:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:The Danish tax reform created a preferential tax scheme for foreign researchers and high-income
28:1055:84650:16:16:71:539:251:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:foreigners.  Instead of the usual top tax rate (of 60%), foreigners were taxed for 3 fiscal years at a flat
28:1056:84757:16:17:71:539:235:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:rate of 30% for their 1991-1995 income and then at another reduced rate of 25% after 1995.  Since
28:1057:84854:17:16:71:539:218:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:our inventors would typically qualify as “researchers,” we can study whether they were affected by
28:1058:84952:16:26:71:148:202:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:this tax scheme.
28:1059:84968:26:16:88:539:176:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:We revert to using the PCT data, since Denmark is essentially not represented in the USPTO
28:1060:85058:16:17:71:539:160:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:data.   Recall  that  in  the  PCT  data,  we  do  not  have  inventor  quality  measures  since  it  is  not  a
28:1061:85170:17:20:71:539:143:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:panel data.  Looking at the effect on all inventors is likely to give us a lower bound of the effects of
28:1062:85274:20:14:80:539:123:6:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f7:F:36The approach puts significant weight on Canada and on Switzerland for the top quality series and on Canada,
28:1063:85383:14:7:72:461:109:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:F:Great Britain, and Japan for the lower quality series (see AppendixD and Appendix tableA12)
28:1064:85474:7:15:80:539:102:6:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f7:F:37Unfortunately, other such reforms, such as the Spanish law of 2004 studied byKleven et al.(2013) took place
28:1065:85583:15:11:72:540:87:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:F:too late given our sample years (and the problem of truncation of patent citations) and cannot be studied well in our
28:1066:85700:11:0:72:102:76:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:F:setting.
29:1067:85762:0:16:72:540:701:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:the reform on the high-quality, high-income inventors.  In addition, we cannot track who is eligible
29:1068:85862:16:22:72:474:685:11:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f5:B:under the 3-year rule.  Overall, this should give us a diluted, or lower-bound effect.38
29:1069:85950:22:17:88:540:663:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:In Figure 9we plot the fraction of foreign inventors in Denmark and in the synthetic country
29:1070:86042:17:16:71:539:646:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:(again normalized by a base year (1985)), as well as the top tax rate differential on foreigners.  We
29:1071:86143:16:16:71:539:630:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:here use as an outcome variable the fraction of foreigners (foreign inventors over all inventors in
29:1072:86242:16:17:71:539:614:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:Denmark), since this allows us to see the differential effect on foreigners (affected by the reform)
29:1073:86342:17:16:71:539:597:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:relative to domestic inventors (not affected by this reform).  The synthetic control algorithm puts
29:1074:86441:16:17:71:539:581:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:a  large  weight  on  Switzerland  and  some  small  weights  on  Canada  and  Portugal  (see  Appendix
29:1075:86544:17:16:71:539:564:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:D), which are the countries in the PCT sample that best match Denmark’s pre-reform share of
29:1076:86635:16:17:71:539:548:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:foreign inventors.  The effects of the Danish reform on the inflow of foreigners is clear relative to the
29:1077:86740:17:16:71:539:531:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:synthetic control.  The implied elasticity is 0.7, which is a bit lower than our preferred elasticity of
29:1078:86844:16:16:71:540:515:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:foreigners in the micro analysis based on the DID in Section5, but almost identical to the elasticity
29:1079:86945:16:40:72:308:499:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:of foreigners based on the EPO data in Section7.

30:1098:88552:0:29:72:343:701:14:g_d0_f2:14:g_d0_f2:C:5    Location Choice Model Estimation
30:1099:88589:29:16:72:540:672:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:In this section, we present the specification of and the results from the multinomial location model
30:1100:88689:16:38:72:343:656:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:estimation that exploits our two identification strategies.
30:1101:88748:38:33:72:271:618:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:C:5.1    Specification and Estimation
30:1102:88783:33:17:72:539:585:11:g_d0_f14:11:g_d0_f3:B:Utility  specification  and  controls:To  model  the  location  choice  of  inventors,  we  adopt  a
30:1103:88883:17:16:71:540:568:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f15:B:multinomial discrete-choice model.  Recall from section 2.2 that inventoriin countrycat timet
30:1104:88976:16:17:71:141:552:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:obtains utility:
30:1105:88992:17:0:236:271:535:11:g_d0_f15:11:g_d0_f15:C:Uict=u
30:1106:88998:0:9:273:278:544:11:g_d0_f21:11:g_d0_f21:?:(
30:1107:88999:9:0:278:342:535:11:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f18:?:(1−τchit)wict
30:1108:89012:0:9:343:348:544:11:g_d0_f21:11:g_d0_f21:?:)
30:1109:89013:9:25:350:540:535:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:+μict(5)
30:1110:89021:25:16:88:539:510:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:For the empirical specification, we assume log utility of consumption (which allows us to rewrite
30:1111:89118:16:17:71:539:494:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:utility as additively separable in pre-tax earnings and the tax rate).  Our benchmark sample for
30:1112:89214:17:16:71:539:477:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:the multinomial analysis contains inventors who, over their lifetime in the sample, have ever been
30:1113:89312:16:17:71:539:461:11:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f5:B:or will ever be classified in the top 25% inventors (according to the ranking defined previously).39
30:1114:89412:17:16:71:539:444:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:Recall that we restrict the sample to the 8 countries which account for around 90% of all patents
30:1115:89509:16:16:71:539:428:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:in the USPTO. Hence, in each year, inventors face a choice between the United States, Canada,
30:1116:89602:16:18:71:380:412:11:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f5:B:Germany, Great Britain, France, Japan, Italy and Switzerland.40
30:1117:89665:18:16:88:539:394:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:An  important  part  of  the  analysis  is  to  model  as  detailed  and  flexibly  as  possible  i)  the  id-
30:1118:89775:16:17:71:540:378:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:iosyncratic  preference  componentμictand  ii)  the  counterfactual  wagewict.   We  consider  them  in
30:1119:89878:17:25:71:95:361:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:turn.
30:1120:89883:25:16:71:539:336:11:g_d0_f14:11:g_d0_f3:B:Controlling for the idiosyncratic preference component:The innovator’s idiosyncratic pref-
30:1121:89973:16:18:71:376:320:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:erence for any given country at timetis assumed to depend on:
30:1122:90034:18:16:88:540:302:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:i)  Individual-level  characteristicsxti:  These  include  the  inventor’s  age,  his  dynamic  quality
30:1123:90137:16:17:71:539:286:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:measure, his technological field, and whether he works in a multinational.  In addition, we include
30:1124:90236:17:16:71:539:269:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:indicator variables for whether the inventor is in the top 1%, top 1-5%, top 5-10%, top 10-25%,
30:1125:90331:16:17:71:540:253:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:or below top 25% of inventors as ranked by quality and explained in section2.3.  The benchmark
30:1126:90425:17:16:71:539:236:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:measure used is the citations-weighted patents to date, but we consider all of the measuresq1−q4
30:1127:90521:16:16:71:539:220:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:from formulas (1)-(4).  The effect of these individual characteristics is allowed to vary by country
30:1128:90621:16:17:71:539:204:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:(i.e., they are all interacted with country fixed effects).  We assign one of six technological fields to
30:1129:90726:17:16:71:540:187:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:the inventor based on the field in which he has most patents.  These six fields that come fromHall
30:1130:90824:16:17:71:540:171:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:et al.(2001) include chemical,  computer and communications,  drugs and medical,  electrical and
30:1131:90920:17:20:71:493:154:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:electronics, mechanical and others.  Using finer classifications did not change our results.
30:1132:91012:20:14:80:539:134:6:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f7:F:39This  is  to  reduce  the  computational  burden  of  the  multinomial  logit  with  many  fixed  effects  on  a  very  large
30:1133:91139:14:11:72:540:120:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:F:sample.  Each inventor-year observation will be duplicated 8 times for each of the 8 potential country choices, thus
30:1134:91255:11:7:72:214:109:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:F:drastically scaling up the data size.
30:1135:91292:7:15:80:540:102:6:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f7:F:40Note that the sample cut is based on a static measure of inventor quality, namely those who haveeverbeen in
30:1136:91401:15:11:72:540:87:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:F:the top 25% in their lifetime, while the ranking within that sample is dynamic and can change for a given inventor
30:1137:91515:11:0:72:510:76:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:F:from year to year.  Table 9 considers how the results change if we also rank inventors by the static measures.
31:1138:91679:0:16:88:539:701:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:ii) Country-level covariates, denoted byxct: These depend on the identification used. In the case

31:1150:92801:16:16:71:539:503:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:country, and a dummy for whether the home and destination country have a common language.
31:1151:92890:16:18:71:268:487:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:These could all affect the ease of moving.
31:1152:92932:18:16:88:539:469:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:In  Section  5.4  that  focuses  on  the  role  of  companies  in  the  migration  decision,  we  also  con-
31:1153:93040:16:17:71:539:453:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:sider other country-inventor specific covariates such as the share of the innovative activity of the
31:1154:93140:17:26:71:299:436:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:inventor’s company in each destination country.
31:1155:93187:26:16:71:540:410:11:g_d0_f14:11:g_d0_f3:B:Controlling for the tax rate:As explained in Section 2.3, we use the top marginal tax rate as
31:1156:93280:16:16:71:539:394:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:our tax measure.  We include the log of the top retention rate interacted with indicator variables
31:1157:93378:16:17:71:540:378:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:for the inventor’s quality rank at timet, denoted byrit, whereritcan be the top 1%, top 1-5%,
31:1158:93471:17:16:71:539:361:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:top 5-10%, top 10-25% or below the top 25%.  In the case of identification 1, which uses country-
31:1159:93568:16:17:71:539:345:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:by-year variation in the top marginal tax rate, this simply allows for differential effects of the top
31:1160:93670:17:16:71:539:328:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:tax rate on different quality inventors.  In the case of identification 2, this captures the propensities
31:1161:93775:16:26:71:383:312:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:of different quality groups of being “treated” by the top tax rate.
31:1162:93842:26:16:71:539:286:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:We hence obtain the econometric specification for a discrete choice model at the individual inventor

31:1177:94845:15:0:72:232:76:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:F:variables which do not vary by country.
32:1178:94920:0:16:88:539:701:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:For  our  preferred  identification  2,  to  compute  the  effect  of  the  top  tax  rate  on  the  top  1%
32:1179:95028:16:17:72:540:685:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:inventors, we need to pick a control group.  As explained previously, given the fuzzy design, it is
32:1180:95127:17:16:72:540:668:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:not a priori obvious which group is the best control group.  This is why we provide the results for

32:1182:95325:16:17:72:540:636:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:that in this estimation sample, the “below top 25%” refers to a still relatively high quality group

32:1186:95692:24:16:72:540:562:11:g_d0_f14:11:g_d0_f3:B:Controlling for the counterfactual wage:As explained earlier, a crucial challenge is to control
32:1187:95787:16:17:72:540:546:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:for the counterfactual wagewctithat inventoriwould receive in any countrycat timet.  Part of the
32:1188:95883:17:16:72:540:529:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:wage variation is well absorbed by the aforementioned controls (i)-(iii), which capture aggregate
32:1189:95980:16:17:72:540:513:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:effects at the country-year level and the technological class level. In addition, we consider three more
32:1190:96084:17:16:72:539:496:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:benchmark specifications that progressively add the following, more detailed proxies for log(wcti).
32:1191:96183:16:17:72:326:480:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:Overall, we estimate the following four specifications:
32:1192:96238:17:17:88:250:463:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:1) Including only controls (i)-(iii).
32:1193:96275:17:17:88:539:446:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:2)  Adding  the  quality  of  the  inventor  at  timet,  interacted  with  country  fixed  effects.   This
32:1194:96381:17:16:72:540:429:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:controls  for  aggregate  country-specific  effects  that  vary  by  ability.   Our  benchmark  measure  is,
32:1195:96489:16:17:72:539:413:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:as explained in Section2.3,  citation-weighted patents to date (measureq1).  Alternative quality
32:1196:96585:17:17:72:368:396:11:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f5:B:measures are considered in the robustness checks in Table9.42
32:1197:96646:17:16:88:539:379:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:3) Adding country and ability specific trends, i.e., controlling for year trend times country fixed
32:1198:96745:16:16:71:539:363:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:effect times the ability measure, in order to capture differential evolutions over time in the wage
32:1199:96844:16:17:71:219:347:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:premium in different countries.
32:1200:96875:17:17:88:539:330:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:4) Adding country, ability and technological field specific trends by controlling for year trend
32:1201:96971:17:24:71:426:313:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:times country fixed effects times ability times technological field dummies.
32:1202:97047:24:17:71:539:289:11:g_d0_f14:11:g_d0_f3:B:Estimation:Denote  byPict≡Prob(Uict> Uic′t,∀c′)  the  probability  of  inventorito  locate  in
32:1203:97141:17:16:72:539:272:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:countrycat timet.  If the error termvicthas a type I extreme value distribution, this model can

34:1356:102922:11:11:72:540:257:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:F:and country-specific  time  trends.   Column 4 contains quality,  country and  technological field  specific time  trends.
