34:1358:103166:11:11:72:540:235:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:F:1% of inventors, while the second row reports the standard error.  The subsequent row pairs report, respectively, the
34:1359:103283:11:11:72:540:224:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:F:coefficients from the retention rate interacted with being in, respectively, the top 1-5%, top 5-10%, top 10-25% and
34:1360:103399:11:11:72:540:213:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:F:below the top 25% of inventors, as well as their standard errors.  “Domestic elasticity” is the elasticity of domestic top
34:1361:103521:11:11:72:540:202:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:F:1% superstar inventors with respect to the top net-of-tax rate (one minus the top tax rate), while “Foreign elasticity”
34:1362:103640:11:11:72:540:191:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:F:is the elasticity of foreign top 1% superstar inventors with respect to the top net-of-tax rate.  They are computed
34:1363:103755:11:39:72:424:180:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:F:according to formulas (9) and (10) with ∆αg=αtop 1%.∗p <0.1,∗∗p <0.05,∗∗∗p <0.01
34:1364:103835:39:32:72:459:141:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:estimates using the below top 25% as a control group in Section5.3and Table5.
34:1365:103912:32:17:88:539:109:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:It is interesting that the top 10-25% and below the top 25% are actually negatively driven by
34:1366:104005:17:16:72:540:92:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:top tax rate decreases, which can be due to the presence of sorting and general equilibrium effects.
34:1367:104105:16:0:72:539:76:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:Indeed, the lack of country×year fixed effects here means that sorting and general equilibrium
35:1368:104253:0:16:72:540:701:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:effects could be loaded on the estimated coefficients on the log retention rate.  The migration of
35:1369:104351:16:17:72:540:685:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:some inventors can have general equilibrium effects and spillovers on other inventors, depending on
35:1370:104450:17:16:72:540:668:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:the structure of the labor market.  For instance, if demand for inventors by companies in different
35:1371:104549:16:16:72:540:652:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:countries  is  rigid,  a  lower  top  tax  rate  could  lead  to  sorting  by  higher  quality  inventors,  to  the
35:1372:104664:16:17:72:539:636:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:detriment of lower quality inventors.44A high influx of top 1% and top 5% inventors may displace
35:1373:104760:17:37:72:191:619:11:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f5:B:lower quality inventors.45
35:1374:104786:37:25:72:540:582:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:F:5.3    Results exploiting the differential effects on inventors of different qualities
35:1375:104872:25:17:72:539:557:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:Table 5contains the estimation results for our main identification that compares the effect of the
35:1376:104970:17:16:72:540:540:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:top  tax  rate  on  the  top  1%  inventors  relative  to  lower  quality  inventors.   The  coefficient  on  the
35:1377:105083:16:17:72:540:524:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:retention rate for the top 1% inventors is significantly positive and large.  The top 1-5% inventors
35:1378:105183:17:16:72:540:507:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:still exhibit a very significantly positive effect of top tax rates, as can be expected since inventors
35:1379:105286:16:17:72:540:491:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:in this group have a very high propensity of being treated.  The top 5-10% inventors also show a
35:1380:105382:17:16:72:540:474:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:positive effect, albeit insignificant, since their propensity to be treated is lower.  The coefficients
35:1381:105485:16:16:72:540:458:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:decline monotonically as we move down the quality distribution due to the declining propensities
35:1382:105581:16:18:72:246:442:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:of being treated by the top tax rate.
35:1383:105618:18:16:88:539:424:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:The lower panel in the table reports the elasticities of domestic top 1% superstar inventors and
35:1384:105714:16:17:72:540:408:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:foreign top 1% superstar inventors for different choices of the control groupg, computed according
35:1385:105812:17:16:72:540:391:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:to  formulas  (9)  and  (10)  forg∈ {top 5-10%, top 10-25%, below top 25%}.   Depending  on  the
35:1386:105908:16:17:72:540:375:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:control group chosen, the estimated elasticities of domestic and foreign inventors will be different.
35:1387:106009:17:16:72:540:358:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:As already discussed above, a control group such as the top 5-10% may give a lower bound estimate,
35:1388:106107:16:16:72:540:342:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:since inventors in this group may still be partially treated.  A control group such as the below top
35:1389:106207:16:17:72:540:326:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:25%, while still a relatively high quality group, has a lower propensity of being treated and will
35:1390:106305:17:16:72:540:309:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:hence yield a larger estimated effect of the top tax rate on superstar top 1% inventors.  For the
35:1391:106402:16:17:72:540:293:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:control group consisting of, respectively, the top 5-10%, the top 10-25%, and the below top 25%,
35:1392:106498:17:16:72:540:276:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:the estimated domestic elasticities are, respectively, 0.02, 0.02, and 0.03 (and are all statistically
35:1393:106600:16:17:72:540:260:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:significant at the 1% level).  The corresponding elasticities on foreign inventors are, respectively,
35:1394:106701:17:17:72:168:243:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:0.63, 0.84, and 1.04.
35:1395:106722:17:16:88:540:226:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:For comparison,Kleven,  Landais,  and Saez (2013)find that,  depending on the specification,
35:1396:106814:16:17:72:540:210:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:the  domestic  elasticity  of  football  players  is  between  0.07  and  0.16,  while  the  foreign  elasticity
35:1397:106926:17:16:72:540:193:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:is between 0.6 and 1.3.  The authors suggested that their elasticities might be upper bounds,  as
35:1398:107023:16:17:72:540:177:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:football players are highly mobile individuals.  In addition, they only consider the European football
35:1399:107125:17:17:72:396:160:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:market, while we also include mobility between different continents.
35:1400:107193:17:20:88:539:143:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:To roughly illustrate these elasticities, suppose that the average country decreases its top tax
35:1401:107289:20:10:80:516:123:6:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f7:A:44Kleven, Landais, and Saez (2013) also explore sorting effects in a rigid demand model for football players.
35:1402:107398:10:15:80:539:113:6:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f7:F:45Another  possible  interpretation  of  the  negative  coefficient  on  lower  quality  inventors,  is  that  there  are  direct
35:1403:107527:15:11:72:540:98:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:F:aggregate effects of the top tax rate through tax revenue, which benefits lower quality inventors.  However, controlling
35:1404:107647:11:11:72:540:87:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:F:for total tax revenue per capita in countrycand timetleaves the effects of the top tax rate on different quality
35:1405:107759:11:0:72:190:76:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:F:inventors entirely unchanged.

37:1486:113040:0:36:267:539:145:11:g_d0_f16:11:g_d0_f3:A:×(εcd×Ndc+εcf×Nfc)×Np×Vp(11)
37:1487:113068:36:18:71:540:109:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:whereεcdandεcfare as defined in equations (7) and (8),NdcandNfcare the number of, respectively,
37:1488:113163:18:15:80:539:91:6:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f7:F:47Note that the heterogeneous elasticities of migration to tax rates across countries could be another reason for
37:1489:113276:15:0:72:320:76:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:F:why some countries can tax more than others (Kleven,2014).
38:1490:113370:0:16:72:540:701:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:domestic and foreign top 1% superstar inventors who live in countryc,Npis the average number
38:1491:113462:16:17:71:540:685:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:of patents per year of top 1% superstar inventors (2.7 in our sample), andVpis the average value
38:1492:113558:17:17:71:124:668:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:per patent.
38:1493:113569:17:16:88:539:651:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:To assign an average value per patent, we use estimates from the literature.Pakes(1985) finds
38:1494:113662:16:16:71:539:635:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:that  the  average  value  of  a  patent  is  $  810,000  (in  1972  dollars),  which  represents  $  2.7  million
38:1495:113776:16:17:71:539:619:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:in 2000 dollars.48Naturally,  this is likely to be a lower bound on the value of the patents from
38:1496:113873:17:16:71:539:602:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:superstar top 1% inventors. Superstar inventors are by definition those who create the most valuable
38:1497:113973:16:17:71:539:586:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:breakthrough patents.  Indeed, while the median patent in our sample receives 8 citations, the most
38:1498:114072:17:16:71:539:569:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:valuable top 1% patents receive on average 171 citations, which is 21 times higher.  Hence, we can
38:1499:114170:16:17:71:539:553:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:perform a second calculation, supposing that the value per patent of superstar top 1% inventors
38:1500:114265:17:16:71:539:536:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:is  close  to  the  value  of  the  top  1%  most  valuable  patents  (which  could  be  approximated  by  21
38:1501:114374:16:16:71:539:520:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:times the average value of $ 2.7 million, i.e., $ 57 million.49)  The potential gains in economic value
38:1502:114477:16:17:71:539:504:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:from top tax decreases are shown in Table7 for a 5 percentage point and a 10 percentage point
38:1503:114570:17:16:71:539:487:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:top  tax  decrease.   Naturally,  these  are  only  the  gains  through  the  migration  channel  of  top  1%
38:1504:114679:16:17:71:539:471:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:inventors and there are of course many other economic gains or losses from reducing the top tax
38:1505:114774:17:16:71:540:454:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:rate through other channels in the rest of the economy.50These effects could also be a lower bound
38:1506:114872:16:17:71:539:438:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:of the economic value lost if there are positive spillovers from having superstar inventors locally
38:1507:114971:17:16:71:540:421:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:(as documented in the papers cited in the Introduction and in Section2.3).  As we show in Section
38:1508:115068:16:16:71:539:405:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:6.1, superstar inventors also have more patent breadth and breadth of impact, above and beyond
38:1509:115162:16:17:71:429:389:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:pure citations, which may imply that their patents are even more valuable.
38:1510:115236:17:17:88:539:372:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:The  economic  gains  per  country  from  decreasing  top  tax  rates  depend  on  the  domestic  and
38:1511:115337:17:16:71:540:355:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:foreign elasticities (in Table6), but also on the size of the inventor base.  The U.S. has the largest
38:1512:115439:16:17:71:539:339:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:economic gain, despite the small elasticities, while Italy has the smallest economic gains, which is
38:1513:115539:17:16:71:539:322:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:a combination of a relatively low elasticity of domestic inventors and a relatively small inventor
38:1514:115637:16:17:71:539:306:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:base.  To a first-order we could imagine that these yearly gains would scale up for a tax decrease
38:1515:115735:17:35:71:183:289:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:that lasts several years.
38:1516:115760:35:25:71:240:254:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:C:5.4    The Role of Companies
38:1517:115788:25:16:71:539:229:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:What is the role of employers in determining inventors’ mobility?  One might expect that role to
38:1518:115884:16:17:71:539:213:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:be important.  Indeed, large companies often recruit internationally.  In the U.S., Qualcomm Inc.
38:1519:115981:17:16:71:539:196:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:and  Microsoft  have  ratio  of  foreign  inventors  to  total  inventors  in  the  company  of,  respectively,
38:1520:116092:16:16:71:539:180:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:51% and 57%.  In Switzerland, Alstom Technology Ltd.  and Syngenta Participation AG both have
38:1521:116185:16:19:71:540:164:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:immigration rates of 67%.51There are two related questions when talking about the role of the
38:1522:116278:19:11:80:508:145:6:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f7:A:48We use the GDP deflator provided by the Bureau of Economic Analysis to adjust the nominal numbers.
38:1523:116378:11:11:80:400:134:6:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f7:A:49Assuming that the value of patents scales approximately linearly in citations.
38:1524:116458:11:14:80:539:123:6:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f7:F:50Because  this  is  clearly  just  a  very  small  fraction  of  all  the  effects  that  lower  top  tax  rates  could  have,  these
38:1525:116592:14:11:72:540:109:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:F:numbers are not meant to be compared to the lost tax revenue.  They are just meant to illustrate the “dollar value”
38:1526:116707:11:7:72:185:98:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:F:of the elasticities estimated.
38:1527:116737:7:15:80:539:91:6:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f22:F:51WIPO  report  available  athttp://www.wipo.int/edocs/pubdocs/en/intproperty/941/wipo_pub_941_2013.

39:1549:117421:11:11:72:539:487:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:F:chosen is the below top 25% of inventors from Table5.  To compute the change in domestic inventors and the change
39:1550:117534:11:11:72:540:476:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:F:in foreign inventors, we consider a 5 and 10 percentage points decrease in top tax rates from the actual tax rate in
39:1551:117650:11:11:72:540:465:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:F:each country.  The economic gain per year is computed as in formula (11).  Columns 1 and 2 assume a patent value
39:1552:117762:11:11:72:540:454:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:F:per superstar top 1% inventor equal to the average patent value of $ 2.7 million.  Columns 3 and 4 assume a large
39:1553:117875:11:11:72:540:443:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:F:patent value equal to $ 57 million.  These values are obtained using patent value estimates fromPakes(1985) and
39:1554:117986:11:11:72:540:432:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:F:our own calculations provided in the text.  These effects could be underestimating the economic value lost if there
39:1555:118101:11:11:72:540:421:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:F:are positive spillovers from having superstar inventors locally (as documented in the papers cited in the Introduction
39:1556:118219:11:38:72:150:410:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:F:and in Section2.3).
39:1557:118238:38:16:72:540:372:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:employer.  The first is whether employer characteristics, in particular whether it is a multinational
39:1558:118339:16:17:72:540:356:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:company and how concentrated it is in some countries, matters. The second is whether the employer
39:1559:118436:17:16:72:540:339:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:contributes to the decision of where to locate and, as a result, the estimated elasticity is a mix of
39:1560:118537:16:17:72:211:323:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:employee and firm responses.
39:1561:118565:17:16:88:539:306:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:Regarding  the  latter  question,  the  top  personal  income  tax  rate  affects  the  surplus  available
39:1562:118671:16:17:72:540:290:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:from a firm-employee match.  Depending on the bargaining setup between firms and employees, the
39:1563:118766:17:16:72:540:273:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:firm should internalize to varying degrees the level of the personal income tax rate.  In the limit, if
39:1564:118869:16:17:72:540:257:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:the firm had to pay full compensating differentials for higher top tax rates to star workers, it should
39:1565:118972:17:16:72:540:240:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:perfectly internalize personal income tax rates.  At the same time, the company might bring to the
39:1566:119070:16:16:72:540:224:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:table other considerations for relocating the worker, which are orthogonal to the personal income
39:1567:119167:16:17:72:540:208:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:tax rate.  In this latter case, the observed sensitivity to the top personal income tax rates should
39:1568:119267:17:16:72:540:191:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:be lowered relative to a case where workers and firms decide unitarily.  To sum up, any observed
39:1569:119363:16:17:72:540:175:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:response to personal income taxes may be driven by the employee or by the firm, depending on the
39:1570:119459:17:16:72:247:158:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:bargaining and wage setting process.
39:1571:119495:16:17:88:539:142:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:Regarding  the  role  of  the  type  of  employer,  in  theory,  the  effects  on  international  mobility
39:1572:119601:17:16:72:540:125:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:of  working  for  a  multinational  company  are  ambiguous.   On  the  one  hand,  it  might  make  an
39:1573:119704:16:17:72:540:109:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:international  move  easier  for  the  worker  either  directly  within  the  company,  or  by  giving  him
39:1574:119811:17:16:72:540:92:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:access to a wider international network built over the course of his career in a multinational.  Of
39:1575:119910:16:0:72:540:76:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:course, workers more likely to take advantage of tax differentials in the future could also simply
40:1576:120044:0:16:72:540:701:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:self-select  into  a  multinational  with  the  expectation  to  move  in  response  to  tax  rates.   On  the
40:1577:120154:16:17:72:540:685:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:other hand, multinationals may be more able to relocate their workers internationally for strategic
40:1578:120253:17:16:72:540:668:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:corporate reasons, rather than because of personal income tax rates, which would tend to dampen
40:1579:120348:16:16:72:540:652:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:the estimated elasticity to top personal tax rates.  The role of companies for inventor mobility is
40:1580:120447:16:43:72:161:636:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:studied in Table 8.

40:1615:121553:11:11:71:539:143:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:F:interaction term of the log retention rate with whether the inventor was employed by a non-multinational company

40:1619:122011:11:10:71:539:99:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:F:and an interaction of the activity share with the top retention rate.  Inventors are significantly less sensitive to the
40:1620:122131:10:8:71:539:89:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:F:top tax rate in any destination country if their company has a large share of its innovative activity in that country.
40:1621:122249:8:0:71:199:81:6:g_d0_f19:9:g_d0_f7:F:∗p <0.1,∗∗p <0.05,∗∗∗p <0.01
41:1622:122331:0:16:88:539:701:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:Column 1 of Table8 reports the results from the benchmark specification, adding the interaction
41:1623:122426:16:17:71:539:685:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:of the top retention rate with a dummy equal to 1 if the inventor didnotwork for a multinational
41:1624:122522:17:16:71:539:668:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:company in the previous period during which he was observed in the sample.  Inventors who are not
41:1625:122619:16:16:71:539:652:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:in multinationals are significantly less sensitive to the top tax rate.  It seems, then, that working
41:1626:122720:16:17:71:435:636:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:for a multinational company facilitates taking advantage of tax differentials.
41:1627:122798:17:16:88:539:619:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:Next, we compute the share of innovative activity of the inventor’s company that takes place in
41:1628:122893:16:17:71:539:603:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:each potential destination country, defined as the fraction of yearly patents of the company assigned
41:1629:122994:17:16:71:539:586:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:to inventors from that country.  Column 2 shows that if the company of the inventor has a higher
41:1630:123090:16:17:71:539:570:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:share of its innovative activities in some destination country, the inventor is less sensitive to the
41:1631:123191:17:16:71:539:553:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:retention rate in that destination country.  The elasticity for those inventors whose company has
41:1632:123288:16:16:71:539:537:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:no share of activity in the foreign country is very large, but declines very rapidly in the share of
41:1633:123388:16:17:71:146:521:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:activity abroad.
41:1634:123404:17:16:88:539:504:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:This does not give us much indication as to who (the employee or the firm) ultimately takes
41:1635:123495:16:17:71:539:488:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:the decision where to locate the worker.  Indeed, a higher activity share abroad might mean that
41:1636:123591:17:16:71:539:471:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:the idiosyncratic preferenceμof the inventor is large for that destination country, due to career
41:1637:123688:16:17:71:539:455:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:concerns, and this difference is sufficiently large to outweigh tax differentials.  But it may instead be
41:1638:123793:17:16:71:539:438:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:the company that wants to relocate inventors to high activity places for strategic corporate reasons
41:1639:123893:16:16:71:539:422:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:unrelated to the personal income tax.  Both scenarios would generate the reduced elasticity to tax
41:1640:123991:16:17:71:202:406:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:rates observed in column 2.
41:1641:124018:17:16:88:539:389:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:While  companies  may  or  may  not  be  relocating  workers  due  to  personal  tax  considerations,
41:1642:124119:16:17:71:539:373:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:we can at least provide some evidence that they do not relocate inventors in our sample based on
41:1643:124215:17:16:71:540:356:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:corporate taxation.  Appendix TableA14reports the results from regressions identical to those in
41:1644:124311:16:17:71:539:340:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:Table4, to which we add the corporate tax as an explanatory variable.  The corporate tax rate has
41:1645:124408:17:16:71:331:323:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:no explanatory power for inventors’ location decisions.
41:1646:124463:16:17:88:539:307:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:Overall, even though we cannot ultimately detect who makes the decision to move, we showed
41:1647:124553:17:38:71:470:290:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:that employer characteristics matter for the elasticity of migration to top tax rates.
41:1648:124639:38:27:71:493:252:14:g_d0_f2:14:g_d0_f2:C:6    Robustness to Alternative Specifications and Extensions
41:1649:124699:27:16:71:539:225:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:This section provides an extensive series of robustness checks on our benchmark results and several
41:1650:124798:16:32:71:123:209:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:extensions.
41:1651:124809:32:24:71:324:177:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:C:6.1    Alternative inventor quality measures
41:1652:124853:24:16:71:539:153:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:Our measure of inventor quality and the corresponding ranking of inventors is central to our analysis.
41:1653:124955:16:28:71:508:137:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:Therefore, we explore here how the results change if we consider different quality measures.
41:1654:125047:28:17:71:539:109:11:g_d0_f14:11:g_d0_f3:B:Static  versus  dynamic  measures,  wage  formation  and  employer  expectations:Recall
41:1655:125134:17:16:71:539:92:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:that our benchmark quality measure is dynamic citations-weighted patents.  This means that an
41:1656:125227:16:0:71:539:76:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:inventor could be classified as a superstar today (if he is ranked in the top of the regional quality
42:1657:125364:0:16:72:540:701:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:distribution in that year), but may not have been a superstar yesterday and may also no longer
42:1658:125458:16:17:72:540:685:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:be a superstar tomorrow.  I.e., dynamic superstar rankings can change over time and it is assumed
42:1659:125555:17:16:72:540:668:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:that only the current quality ranking matters for income.  This corresponds to a situation in which
42:1660:125654:16:16:72:540:652:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:the employer has no foresight at all about the inventor’s future potential or there are no job search
42:1661:125755:16:17:72:540:636:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:and matching frictions that would prevent firms from firing a worker and hiring a better one in a
42:1662:125852:17:16:72:540:619:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:future period in which information about the inventor’s quality is revealed.  Symmetrically, it also
42:1663:125952:16:17:72:540:603:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:implies that, conditional on the current value of the quality measure and rank, past rankings do
42:1664:126048:17:17:72:127:586:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:not matter.
42:1665:126059:17:16:88:539:569:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:Of  course,  the  wage  setting  process  is  a  complicated  one  and  might  depend  both  on  past
42:1666:126160:16:17:72:540:553:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:performance  and  future  expectations,  which  provide  the  employer  with  additional  information
42:1667:126261:17:16:72:540:536:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:about the inventor’s productivity not necessarily reflected in his current patents to date.  To take a
42:1668:126363:16:17:72:540:520:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:concrete example from academia, a university might hire a promising young Ph.D. graduate without
42:1669:126459:17:16:72:540:503:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:any publication or patent record, based on his revealed skills during conversations and seminars.
42:1670:126556:16:16:72:540:487:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:This new hire may have a high marginal product as measured by his impact on graduate students
42:1671:126649:16:17:72:540:471:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:and colleagues that is not yet reflected in his publication record.  Alternatively, a senior professor
42:1672:126751:17:16:72:540:454:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:with several very high impact publications, but who is no longer producing at a level that would
42:1673:126847:16:17:72:540:438:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:classify  him in  the  current top  1%  of researchers is  probably still  highly  paid based  on his  past
42:1674:126954:17:17:72:105:421:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:record.
42:1675:126961:17:16:88:539:404:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:If these situations apply in practice, a more appropriate component of the income of an inventor
42:1676:127057:16:17:72:540:388:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:would be based on a lifetime, static quality. In particular, we can redefine an inventor as being in the
42:1677:127161:17:16:72:540:371:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:top 1% of inventors if, over the course of his life in the sample, he has ever been or will ever be in the
42:1678:127267:16:17:72:539:355:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:top 1%.  The results for this alternative quality measure are in column 1 of Table9.  The elasticity
42:1679:127367:17:16:72:539:338:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:measures are very close to the benchmark (column 4 in Table5).  In reality, wages are probably set
42:1680:127465:16:16:72:540:322:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:to some extent based on current marginal product and to some extent based on potential future
42:1681:127558:16:17:72:540:306:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:information and on realized past information, especially if there are search and matching frictions
42:1682:127657:17:16:72:540:289:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:that make the employer want to lock in promising employees.  It is hence reassuring that even a
42:1683:127752:16:17:72:317:273:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:fully static measure still maintains our main result.
42:1684:127805:17:17:88:539:256:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:We  also  consider  the  case  in  which  an  inventor  is  defined  as  a  superstar  if  he  has  ever  been
42:1685:127915:17:16:72:539:239:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:in the top 1%in the past(even if he currently no longer is in the top 1%).  This corresponds to
42:1686:128010:16:17:72:540:223:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:the case in which an inventor is always rewarded for past success, even independent of his current
42:1687:128108:17:16:72:540:206:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:performance,  but  is  not  rewarded  in  anticipation  of  future  success,  or  there  is  no  advance,  lead
42:1688:128219:16:17:72:540:190:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:information about the inventor.  The results are almost perfectly identical to the static measure in
42:1689:128319:17:31:72:365:173:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:column 1 of Table9 and hence not reported to save on space.
42:1690:128378:31:17:72:539:142:11:g_d0_f14:11:g_d0_f3:B:Patent quality versus quantity measures:As described in section2.3, there are several pos-
42:1691:128468:17:16:72:540:125:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:sible quality measures based on patents and citations that put different emphasis on the quality
42:1692:128564:16:17:72:540:109:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:versus the quantity of patents.  The correlations of these various measures, although significantly
42:1693:128663:17:16:72:539:92:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:positive at the 5% level, are not always large.  For instance, the correlation between measureq1
42:1694:128759:16:0:71:539:76:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:(citations-weighted patents) andq2 (number of patents) is 0.70, the correlation betweenq1 andq3
43:1695:128908:0:20:217:390:698:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f8:C:Table 9: Robustness Checks

43:1724:130162:16:11:72:540:300:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:F:Notes:  Multinomial logit regressions.  Robust standard errors clustered at the inventor level in parentheses.  See the
43:1725:130281:11:11:72:540:289:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:F:notes  to  Table  5.   All  regressions  contain  the  same  covariates  as  Table5,  column  4.   Column  1  uses  the  lifetime
43:1726:130410:11:11:72:540:278:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:F:measure of inventor ranking (“has ever been or will ever be in the top 1%,” etc..).  The next three columns use three
43:1727:130527:11:11:72:540:267:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:F:alternative  quality  measures  to  rank  inventors  into  the  top  1%,  top  1-5%,  etc..   Column  2  uses  the  patent  count
43:1728:130656:11:11:72:539:256:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:F:to date (measureq2 as defined by formula (2)).  Column 3 uses the inventor’s average citations per patent to date
43:1729:130769:11:11:71:539:245:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:F:(measureq3 as defined in (3)).  Column 4 uses the max citations per patent of an inventor to date (measureq4 as
43:1730:130880:11:11:71:539:234:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:F:defined in (4)).  Column 5 is based on a balanced panel, where an inventor’s location for years in between patents is
43:1731:130997:11:37:71:437:223:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:F:imputed according to the procedure described in the text.∗p <0.1,∗∗p <0.05,∗∗∗p <0.01
43:1732:131082:37:17:71:539:186:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:(average citations per patent) is 0.32 and the correlation betweenq2 andq3 is only 0.05 (see the
43:1733:131178:17:27:72:294:169:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:full correlation matrix in Appendix TableA1).
43:1734:131223:27:17:88:539:142:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:We  may  be  worried  that  our  benchmark  quality  measure  (citations-weighted  patent,q1)  is
43:1735:131320:17:16:71:539:125:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:correlated with the likelihood of observing an inventor in the sample, and, consequently, with the
43:1736:131418:16:17:71:540:109:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:likelihood of observing a move.  Therefore, we provide three more tests by using patent counts (q2),
43:1737:131518:17:16:71:540:92:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:average citations per patent (q3), and max citations per patent (q4) as alternative measures to show
43:1738:131618:16:0:71:539:76:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:that it is really the quality of an inventor that matters, rather than the pure quantity of patents.
44:1739:131754:0:16:72:539:701:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:Column 2 of Table 9reassures us that the results are not artificially driven by observing people with
44:1740:131855:16:17:72:540:685:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:more patents more frequently.  Using simple patent counts, the coefficient on the top retention rate
44:1741:131955:17:16:72:540:668:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:becomes much smaller and insignificant for top 1% inventors, while positive and significant for the
44:1742:132054:16:16:72:540:652:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:below top 25% inventors.  On the other hand, using purely quality driven measures such as average
44:1743:132151:16:17:72:540:636:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:citations per patent (in column 3) or max citations per patent (in column 4), maintains or even
44:1744:132246:17:16:72:540:619:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:strengthens our benchmark results.  Hence, the relation is not mechanically driven by frequency of
44:1745:132344:16:30:72:129:603:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:observation.
44:1746:132356:30:16:72:540:573:11:g_d0_f14:11:g_d0_f3:B:Patent breadth and breadth of impact measures:Another way to assess an inventor’s impact
44:1747:132444:16:16:72:540:557:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:is through the breadth of his innovations, and the extent of his new and original ideas.  We hence
44:1748:132542:16:17:72:540:541:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:construct two additional quality measures.  The first measure, which we call “breadth of impact”
44:1749:132638:17:16:72:540:524:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:considers the number of technology classes that end up building on an inventor’s patents.  Formally,
44:1750:132738:16:17:72:539:508:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:we take the set of patents of an inventor until timet−1 and count the number of technological
44:1751:132831:17:16:71:539:491:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:classes  which  contain  patents  that  ever  cite  those  patents.   The  second  measure,  called  patent
44:1752:132938:16:17:71:539:475:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:breadth,  is  the  dynamic  claims-adjusted  patent  stock,  i.e.,  the  number  of  claims  on  all  patents
44:1753:133047:17:16:71:540:458:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:received by the inventor by timet−1 (constructed exactly as our benchmark measureq1, but using
44:1754:133141:16:17:71:539:442:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:claims instead of citations).  It is common in the literature to use patent claims to proxy for patent
44:1755:133243:17:16:71:539:425:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:breadth (Lerner,1994;Lanjouw and Schankerman,2004).  In Appendix TableA10, we show that,
44:1756:133331:16:16:71:539:409:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:as expected, superstar inventors according to our benchmark definition, also have significantly more
44:1757:133431:16:17:71:539:393:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:patent breadth and breadth of impact.  The results using the breadth of impact and the patent
44:1758:133524:17:33:71:443:376:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:breadth as quality measures are, respectively, in columns 1 and 2 of Table10.
44:1759:133601:33:24:71:301:343:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:C:6.2    Accounting for potential selection
44:1760:133642:24:16:71:539:319:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:One  problem  about  using  the  patent  data  to  track  inventors’  locations  is  that  we  only  observe
44:1761:133750:16:17:71:539:303:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:inventors  in  years  in  which  they  patent,  but  not  in  the  years  between  consecutive  patents.   We
44:1762:133859:17:16:71:539:286:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:perform two analyses to address this problem.  First, we make sure that the results do not change
44:1763:133956:16:17:71:539:270:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:much when we impute the inventors’ locations for missing years.  Second, we estimate a selection
44:1764:134052:17:23:71:103:253:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:model.
44:1765:134058:23:16:71:540:230:11:g_d0_f14:11:g_d0_f3:B:Imputing location for missing years:To impute observations for years in which inventors do
44:1766:134148:16:17:71:539:214:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:not  patent,  we  use  the  following  imputation  algorithm:  if  the  inventor  is  seen  in  countryAin
44:1767:134254:17:16:71:540:197:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:yearXand  in  countryBin  yearY > X,  we  assume  that  he  has  been  in  countryAuntil  year
44:1768:134348:16:16:71:539:181:11:g_d0_f15:11:g_d0_f3:B:X+ (Y−X)/2 and in countryBthereafter and until yearY.  We do not impute years before the
44:1769:134436:16:17:71:540:165:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:first or after the last patent.  Column 5 of Table9 shows that the elasticities are slightly smaller,
44:1770:134537:17:23:71:322:148:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:but still very similar when we use the imputed data.
44:1771:134589:23:16:71:539:125:11:g_d0_f14:11:g_d0_f3:B:Binary Selection Model:To check for selection based on the number of patents, we also use a
44:1772:134680:16:17:71:539:109:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:formal selection model.  To simplify the computational burden, we only study the mobility between
44:1773:134777:17:16:71:539:92:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:the U.S. and Canada.  The U.S.-Canada corridor is very large and among inventors who migrate
44:1774:134869:16:0:71:539:76:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:within this corridor, very few also migrate to another country.  Among 863,406 U.S.-born inventors,
45:1775:135022:0:20:148:457:698:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f8:C:Table 10: Breadth of Impact and Patent Breadth

45:1809:136325:16:21:72:313:216:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:observed both in the U.S. and some third country.
45:1810:136374:21:16:88:539:195:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:First, we estimate a simple probit model for the inventors born and observed only in Canada
45:1811:136465:16:17:72:540:179:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:or  the  U.S.,  where  the  dependent  variable  takes  the  value  1  if  an  inventor  locates  in  the  U.S.
45:1812:136576:17:16:72:540:162:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:The  dependent  variables  are  analogous  to  the  ones  described  in  Section5.1,  with  some  small
45:1813:136679:16:17:72:540:146:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:modifications.  Again, we include the same set of controls i)-iii), and we consider progressively more
45:1814:136781:17:16:72:540:129:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:detailed specifications for the counterfactual wages,  by adding quality measures,  quality-country
45:1815:136880:16:17:72:540:113:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:specific trends and quality-country-field specific trends.  The retention rate is the U.S. top retention
45:1816:136984:17:20:72:368:96:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:rate, interacted with inventor rankings (top 1%, top 1-5%, ..).
45:1817:137047:20:0:88:539:76:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:Next, we perform a formal Heckman selection model with exactly the same controls and compare
46:1818:137175:0:16:72:540:701:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:its results with those from the simple probit model without selection.  We exploit a reform enacted
46:1819:137274:16:17:72:540:685:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:in 1995 and introduced by the “Patent Term and Publication Reform Act of 1994” to synchronize
46:1820:137367:17:16:72:540:668:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:patent terms with requirements of the Uruguay Round Agreements Act.  The main changes were
46:1821:137457:16:16:72:540:652:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:that the patent term of 17 years (counted from the patent grant year) was changed to 20 years from
46:1822:137555:16:17:72:540:636:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:the patent’s earliest application year.  Given that on average the patent grant period is less than
46:1823:137654:17:16:72:540:619:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:3 years, this is typically an effective increase in the patent term.  Indeed, the average lag between
46:1824:137755:16:17:72:540:603:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:the application and the grant was 2 years, which effectively implies that the reform has increased
46:1825:137853:17:16:72:539:586:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f16:B:the average duration of patent protection upon patent grant by 1 year to 18 years (=20 years−
46:1826:137946:16:17:72:540:570:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:2 years).  Appendix Table A9 provides the average gap between the application and grant years
46:1827:138039:17:16:72:540:553:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:on average, as well as for inventors of different qualities and industries.  This reform increased the
46:1828:138141:16:16:72:539:537:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:likelihood of patenting, and, hence, of observing inventors in the data (see Table11below), but
46:1829:138236:16:17:72:540:521:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:should not have affected location choices.  Hence, we use a dummy for post-1994 in the first stage
46:1830:138334:17:18:72:180:504:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:of our selection model.
46:1831:138357:18:16:88:540:486:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:Table11shows the results from the simple probit model and the corresponding selection model.
46:1832:138449:16:41:72:517:470:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:It confirms that the effects of top tax rates remain very similar after controlling for selection.

46:1856:139618:21:16:88:539:92:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:To sum up, the results using imputed data showed that imputing missing years leaves the results
46:1857:139713:16:0:72:540:76:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:highly significant (Table9, column 5).  The results from section6.1using patent count as a quality
47:1858:139865:0:16:72:540:701:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:measure showed that the relation between patenting and moving was not mechanical.  Combined
47:1859:139956:16:17:72:540:685:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:with  the  formal  selection  model  results,  this  tends  to  show  that  selection  based  on  patenting  is
47:1860:140067:17:28:72:236:668:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:likely not the driver of our results.
47:1861:140104:28:16:72:540:640:11:g_d0_f14:11:g_d0_f3:B:Sample  selection:One  might  be  worried  that  the  choice  of  patenting  in  the  USPTO  is  not
47:1862:140204:16:17:72:540:624:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:innocuous for foreign inventors.  First, it could be that inventors who plan to migrate to the U.S.
47:1863:140303:17:16:72:540:607:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:tend to patent more heavily with the USPTO. This would tend to make the observed sample more
47:1864:140395:16:17:72:540:591:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:mobile on average than a fictitious sample in which inventors are randomly assigned to patent offices.
47:1865:140497:17:16:72:540:574:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:On the other hand, however, conditional on appearing in the sample, those who had planned to
47:1866:140589:16:17:72:540:558:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:migrate to the U.S. (and, accordingly, had decided to patent with the USPTO) may not be driven
47:1867:140683:17:16:72:540:541:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:at all by tax considerations, which would tend to reduce the elasticity to taxes.  To address this
47:1868:140781:16:16:72:540:525:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:issue we first repeat the analysis on inventors who patent with the EPO. Many more inventors in
47:1869:140876:16:17:72:540:509:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:the EPO data are Europeans.  These results are presented in Section 7 and confirm our previous
47:1870:140970:17:16:72:540:492:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:results.   Second,  we  drop  all  movers  to  the  U.S.  from  both  the  USPTO  and  the  EPO  samples.
47:1871:141075:16:17:72:540:476:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:These results are reported in Appendix Tables A15 and A17.  These tables show that the effect of
47:1872:141171:17:43:72:460:459:11:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f5:B:the top retention rate is still very significant on the superstar top 1% inventors.52
47:1873:141256:43:28:72:219:416:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:C:6.3    Long-term Mobility
47:1874:141281:28:16:72:540:388:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:The mobility of inventors has different economic implications if it is short-term versus long-term.  In
47:1875:141384:16:16:72:540:372:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:this section, we consider the effects of taxation exclusively on long-term mobility.  We define a long-
47:1876:141487:16:17:72:540:356:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:term move as a move that is never followed by a move back to the origin country during the time the
47:1877:141586:17:16:72:540:339:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:inventor is in the sample.  Recall that the average time in the benchmark sample for an inventor is
47:1878:141685:16:17:72:540:323:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:12 years.  On the one hand, long-term mobility may be much less sensitive to contemporaneous tax
47:1879:141781:17:16:72:540:306:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:rates, since people should normally re-optimize only once future tax changes happen.  On the other
47:1880:141879:16:17:72:540:290:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:hand, long-term mobility could be even more strongly correlated with tax changes if tax changes
47:1881:141974:17:16:72:540:273:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:are highly persistent and people are aware of this fact, or if people overestimate the persistence of
47:1882:142075:16:16:72:540:257:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:tax changes and are then faced with moving costs that prevent them from moving back during the
47:1883:142169:16:17:72:539:241:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:average period of 12 years that we observe them.  The results in column 1 of Table12show that
47:1884:142262:17:16:71:539:224:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:domestic inventors’ long-term mobility is slightly less sensitive to tax rates.  For foreign inventors,
47:1885:142365:16:17:71:539:208:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:it is slightly more sensitive to tax rates.  When it comes to long-term moves, it does not seem to
47:1886:142463:17:16:71:539:191:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:matter significantly whether the inventor works for a multinational (column 2).  It still seems to
47:1887:142561:16:17:71:539:175:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:matter how concentrated the research activity of the employer is (column 3), although the effects
47:1888:142658:17:24:71:534:158:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:are weakened.  This may indicate that for long-term mobility career concerns continue to matter.
47:1889:142754:24:14:80:539:134:6:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f7:F:52Note that for the USPTO sample, overall the estimated coefficients are larger, but the elasticities for domestic
47:1890:142868:14:11:72:540:120:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:F:superstar inventors are a bit smaller and the elasticities of foreign superstar inventors are a bit larger.  This is due
47:1891:142988:11:11:72:540:109:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:F:to the lower overall number of moves once we drop moves to the U.S. (see our discussion of how the elasticities are
47:1892:143103:11:11:72:540:98:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:F:derived from the multinomial logit as in (9) and (10) and related to the probability of staying in one’s home country).
47:1893:143222:11:11:72:540:87:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:F:For the EPO data described in Section 7, there is barely any change at all in the estimated elasticities of domestic
47:1894:143338:11:0:72:540:76:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:F:superstar inventors from dropping movers to the U.S., and an increase in the elasticity of foreign superstar inventors.

48:1933:145173:28:28:71:332:187:14:g_d0_f2:14:g_d0_f2:C:7    European Patent Office Inventors
48:1934:145210:28:17:71:539:159:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:All our micro results until now used the DID, derived from the USPTO data.  This data is naturally
48:1935:145308:17:16:71:539:142:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:heavily dominated by U.S. inventors.  Therefore, it is very valuable to test whether the sensitivity of
48:1936:145411:16:17:71:539:126:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:superstar inventors to top tax rates also holds in the European Patent Office (hereafter, EPO) data.
48:1937:145511:17:16:71:539:109:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:The disambiguation of the EPO data has only recently been done and is the subject of on-going
48:1938:145604:16:17:71:506:93:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:research efforts (seeCoffano and Tarasconi(2014),Breschi, Lissoni, and Tarasconi (2014)).
48:1939:145693:17:0:88:539:76:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:In this data, the representation of the same 8 countries we used for our benchmark analysis is
49:1940:145841:0:16:72:540:701:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:as follows:  Canada accounts for 1.3%, Switzerland for 3.3%, Germany for 23.7%, France for 7.7%,
49:1941:145937:16:17:72:540:685:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:Great Britain for 6.2%, Italy for 3.8%, Japan for 16.4% and the U.S. for 27.5%.  Hence, the biggest
49:1942:146036:17:16:72:540:668:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:difference is the reduced share of the U.S. in the data.  The construction of all variables and the
49:1943:146135:16:16:72:540:652:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:sample is the same as for the benchmark analysis.  For consistency, we also consider the exact same
49:1944:146234:16:17:72:540:636:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:8 countries.  Appendix Table A11 provides some summary statistics for the European patent office
49:1945:146330:17:17:72:279:619:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:data.  The sample period here is 1977-2007.

50:1987:148887:16:17:72:539:685:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:patents (q1).  We see the same pattern as in the DID with the superstar top 1% inventors very sig-
50:1988:148985:17:16:72:540:668:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:nificantly sensitive to top tax rates.  The elasticities of both domestic and foreign superstar top 1%
50:1989:149087:16:16:72:540:652:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:inventors are somewhat smaller than in the DID. Indeed, in the EPO, even the top 5-10% inventors
50:1990:149183:16:17:72:540:636:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:are significantly sensitive to top tax rates, probably because top tax brackets are in general lower
50:1991:149283:17:16:72:540:619:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:in European countries (which are naturally more heavily represented in the EPO than in the DID).
50:1992:149379:16:17:72:540:603:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:Using the top 10-25% and the below top 25% as control groups, yields, respectively, elasticities of
50:1993:149478:17:16:72:540:586:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:domestic top 1% superstar inventors of 0.014 and 0.02 and elasticities of foreign top 1% superstar
50:1994:149576:16:17:72:198:570:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:inventors of 0.67 and 0.76.
50:1995:149603:17:16:88:539:553:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:The next four columns consider the alternative quality measures already shown for the DID in

50:1997:149793:17:16:72:540:520:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:the top 1%,” etc...)  as described in Section6.1.  Column 3 shows the average citations per patent
50:1998:149891:16:16:72:539:504:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:(measureq3), while column 4 shows the max citations per patent (measureq4).  As was the case in
50:1999:149986:16:17:72:540:488:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:the benchmark DID as well, ranking inventors according to their max citations per patent (measure
50:2000:150083:17:16:72:540:471:11:g_d0_f15:11:g_d0_f3:B:q4) yields the strongest elasticities for domestic top 1% superstar inventors of,  respectively 0.02
50:2001:150183:16:17:72:540:455:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:and 0.032 depending on the control group.  Column 5 reports the results for the pure patent count,
50:2002:150281:17:16:72:540:438:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:for which, as explained in Section6.1, it is a very good sign that the effects of the top retention
50:2003:150380:16:17:72:293:422:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:rate on superstar inventors are not significant.
50:2004:150428:17:16:88:539:405:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:In  Online  Appendix  TableA17,  we  provide  the  aforementioned  results  with  the  EPO  data,
50:2005:150525:16:17:72:540:389:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:dropping all inventors who ever move to the U.S..  The effect of the top tax rate on superstar top
50:2006:150623:17:16:72:271:372:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:1% inventors remains strongly significant.
50:2007:150665:16:17:88:539:356:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:Overall, the results using the EPO data are highly consistent with those using the benchmark
50:2008:150757:17:16:72:540:339:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:DID, which gives further confidence in our estimated effects of the top tax rate on superstar top
50:2009:150854:16:39:72:136:323:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:1% inventors.
50:2010:150867:39:27:72:173:284:14:g_d0_f2:14:g_d0_f2:C:8    Conclusion
50:2011:150882:27:17:72:540:257:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:In this paper, we consider the effects of taxation on the international mobility of inventors, who
50:2012:150980:17:16:72:540:240:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:are economically highly valuable agents and key drivers of economic growth.  We put particular
50:2013:151074:16:17:72:540:224:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:emphasis on superstar inventors, those with the most and most valuable inventions.  We use dis-
50:2014:151169:17:16:72:540:207:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:ambiguated inventor data, based on USPTO and EPO data, to track the international location of
50:2015:151262:16:16:72:540:191:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:inventors over time, and combine it with effective top marginal tax rate data.  We exploit varia-
50:2016:151359:16:17:72:540:175:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:tions in the top tax rate across time and countries, as well as its differential impact on inventors
50:2017:151459:17:16:72:288:158:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:at different points in the quality distribution.
50:2018:151507:16:17:88:539:142:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:We first provided stylized macroeconomic facts that highlight the responses of superstar inven-
50:2019:151602:17:16:72:540:125:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:tors to top taxes.  We then presented quasi-experimental evidence from three country case studies
50:2020:151699:16:17:72:540:109:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:that  exploited  large  changes  in  migration  policies  or  tax  policy.   We  estimate  a  multinomial  lo-
50:2021:151809:17:16:72:540:92:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:cation model and find that the baseline elasticity of the number of superstar domestic inventors
50:2022:151905:16:0:72:540:76:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:to the top net-of-tax rate is small (around 0.03 in our preferred specification).  This translates on
51:2023:152008:0:16:72:540:701:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:average into an increase of 1% in domestic superstar top 1% inventors at home for a 10 percentage
51:2024:152105:16:17:72:540:685:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:points  decrease  in  top  tax  rates  from  a  level  of  60%.   The  elasticity  of  the  number  of  superstar
51:2025:152218:17:16:72:540:668:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:top 1% foreign inventors to the net-of-tax rate is much higher, around 1, which translates into a
51:2026:152315:16:16:72:540:652:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:26% increase in foreign superstar top 1% inventors for the same 10 percentage points decrease in
51:2027:152411:16:17:72:540:636:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:top tax rates.  Inventors who have worked for multinationals in the previous period are more likely
51:2028:152510:17:16:72:540:619:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:to take advantage of tax differentials, possibly because working for a multinational makes a move
51:2029:152607:16:17:72:540:603:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:abroad easier and grants the inventor international exposure.  On the other hand, inventors whose
51:2030:152704:17:16:72:540:586:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:company has a research activity that is highly concentrated in a given country are less sensitive
51:2031:152801:16:17:72:540:570:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:to tax differentials in that country, presumably because career concerns (being located where the
51:2032:152898:17:16:72:540:553:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:company’s main research activity is) outweigh tax considerations.  We also find evidence for sorting
51:2033:152998:16:17:72:468:537:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:effects by ability and negative spillovers from high quality to low quality inventors.
51:2034:153084:17:16:88:539:520:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:We  then  perform  extensive  robustness  checks  on  the  measures  of  earnings  and  quality  used,
51:2035:153186:16:17:72:540:504:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:the length of the migration spells studied, and potential selection based on patenting behavior.  In
51:2036:153286:17:16:72:540:487:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:these extensions and robustness checks, our results persist.  We also reproduce the analysis on a
51:2037:153383:16:17:72:540:471:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:new  disambiguated  inventor  dataset  based  on  European  Patent  Office  patents  and  find  baseline
51:2038:153487:17:16:72:540:454:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:elasticities to the net-of-tax rate of 0.02 for domestic top 1% superstar inventors and of 0.76 for
51:2039:153586:16:17:72:240:438:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:foreign top 1% superstar inventors.
51:2040:153621:17:16:88:539:421:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:These results suggest that, if the economic contribution of these key agents is very important,
51:2041:153716:16:17:72:540:405:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:their migratory responses to tax policy might represent a cost to tax progressivity.  Our estimates
51:2042:153815:17:16:72:540:388:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:could fruitfully be used to calibrate the models of optimal taxation in the presence of migration
51:2043:153912:16:16:72:540:372:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:cited in the Introduction.  An additional relevant consideration is that inventors may have strong
51:2044:154010:16:17:72:540:356:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:spillover effects on their geographically close peers, making it even more important to attract and
51:2045:154109:17:17:72:193:339:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:retain them domestically.
51:2046:154134:17:16:88:539:322:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:Because inventors are key determinants of economic growth, this paper speaks to the relation
51:2047:154226:16:17:72:540:306:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:between taxation and growth.  An interesting direction for future research would be to include the
51:2048:154324:17:16:72:540:289:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:migration margin of inventors, together with their externalities, into a structural economic growth
51:2049:154423:16:40:72:172:273:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:model with taxation.
